when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些事 , 但真正重要的是 , 她說的未來將遠遠超過這一點 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個人出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 他又發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都來自數學的觀點 , 但是turing告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 你如何製造電腦並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你的電腦是不是機械的 , 像是babbage的 , 或是像今天的電腦 , 或未來的電路 , 都不管是細胞 , 或是說 , 同樣地 , 機械性的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它做得很小 。 所有的東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教會 」 理論 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 說這個東西babbage真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能做到我們現今用電腦所做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	讓你知道它的速度有多慢 , 有1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡片 , 可以輸入 , 它跑了大約一萬倍的速度--第一張zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一堆零件 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加入更多的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這又帶給我們什麼啟示呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 還有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由charlesbabbage寫 , 內容是關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一套計畫 , 我們稱之為28計劃 , 這也是我和doronswade一起創立的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算器 , 也是驅動這個計劃的人 , 來建造一個不一樣的引擎 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有很多部分要做 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是掃描babbage的檔案庫 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計劃來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是對那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是對科學博物館進行實體建構 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於可以了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有個小晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我聞起來可能很臭 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要進行模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫道:一旦分析引擎存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學方向 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造它 , 因為他總是在磨練新的計劃 , 但在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我給你們看看它在動態中看起來是什麼樣子的影片 , 影片只顯示出cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪 , 加上去 。 這是加入的動作 , 你可以想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	給我五年時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們將擁有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個充滿影像的演講中 , 雅納•亞瑟伯特蘭為他三項最近的作品展現了他的人性以及我們在他系列中的空氣拍攝照片 。 《地球起源》 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談中 , 探討了他的網路專案《六十億人》 , 以及他很快的電影《家》 , 這部紀錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過拍攝影片來記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅納•亞瑟伯特蘭以寬闊的角度捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以搭飛機來這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡要談生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳就跟法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵銷我的碳 , 每次我都要這麼做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展現出我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 關於我去年拍攝的最後幾張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達沙石油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題所在 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們不停地工作 , 七個小時就七個小時 , 盡可能多提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們都知道石油末日 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量比我們發現的還多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	一百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年前就因為全球暖化而被消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感對海洋的生物多樣性也非常重要

it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的方式
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自從1960年起 , 北極的厚度下降了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , 吉利馬扎羅有了新的面貌 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 一百年後 , 所有山上的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命來說是很重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾跟你說的 , 有20億人住在水裡 , 住在喜馬拉雅冰河 。

one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類依賴魚類生存 。

these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年的歷史 。

for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我密切地看著地球和它的居民從高空飛上來 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和地球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、農業 , 仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們聯繫在一起的遠遠遠大於分裂我們的 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們對地球的天賦都有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻繼續築起牆壁 , 使我們彼此隔離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在短短50年間 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 遠遠超出了人類的歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上有一半的森林已經消失 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運行速度很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富落差正在擴大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有意識到 , 地球的生存速度比地球快很多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現在就有解決方案了 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 讓它更好 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克揭示了將如何降低健康照護的便宜和快速基因序列 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 技術 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•瑞斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我會介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的副本 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 還有一小份y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組 , 你就會看到這個雙螺旋結構生命的代碼是用四個生物化學字母拼出來的 , 或是我們稱之為基礎:a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	大家都可以隨意丟出很大的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但實際上 , 如果我把這1280到800個解析度螢幕上的每個像素的一個鹼基 , 我們會需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便一提 , 有一群人決定要排列它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最終的版本出版了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基地的成本大約是一美元 , 非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們拿取一個基因組 , 複製大約50份 , 我們把這些基因切成50鹼基讀取 , 然後我們對它們進行大規模的排序 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體裡 , 把它重新組合起來 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看一下這是什麼樣子的 , 人體基因組計畫:3gabas , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器運行的:一週兩百億美金 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	到了今年夏天 , 兩百人會改變到六百人 , 沒有這種步調緩慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	為一個基對排序的價格已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等同於你在1998年裝滿汽油 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車回木星和兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊式的定序方式 , 還有許多新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數尺度 , 你通常不會看到像這樣上升的線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	全世界對人類基因組進行排序的能力今年大約是五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們是依據機器運輸來的 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期未來會加倍、三倍 , 或四倍之多 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個特別的實驗室 , 代表了所有這些能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因體研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國人在為新月球贏得比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	對醫學而言 , 這意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她會帶著第二期的雌激素受體陽性乳癌來做檢測 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她復發了三期卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她42歲 , 有更多的卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著嚴重的肌肉白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後她過世了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位婦女在短短10年內被治療的方式 , 會看起來像在血液中 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	由於像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定去看這位女子的後遺體 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他進行了基因組定序 , 他採用了皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚、以及癌症的骨髓 , 並在幾週內完成了兩組基因組的排序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩組基因組放在軟體中 , 他發現 , 除了其他東西之外 , 有一個兩千個鹼基在三十億個特定基因中的一個基因 , 叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的基因中有這種致命的突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒什麼幫助 , 但對她的家人來說 , 它的確有很嚴重、很深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果它們有相同的突變 , 它們會得到基因測試 , 它們會去做定期的篩檢 , 它們會早期發現癌症 , 可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹beery雙胞胎在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信這些症狀並不相符 , 透過一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她說服了醫界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是雙重回應的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們服用了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但不是完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的先生 , 名叫joebeery , 他很幸運能成為一家名為 「 生命科技 」 的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造大量基因定序工具的兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是為他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變發生在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 負責產生血清素的基因 , 和其他的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	除此之外 , 他們還給這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥物 , 現在他們已經很正常了 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因定序 , 這不可能發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 當時的價格是十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	比方說 , 美金一百元 , 或一年後
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動速度的快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和噴射槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	nick出現在兒童醫院裡 , 像受害者一樣 , 腹部會很不一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西 , 他的腸道基本上會向外敞開 , 糞便會溢出到他的腸道中 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我真的很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因組定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現的是控制細胞死亡的基因中一個單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論是 , 他對食物本質的反應有一些免疫反應 , 那是自然的反應 , 導致細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制下來的基因是破碎的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這就表示 , 除了治療骨髓移植手術之外 , 他還接受了骨髓移植 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	九個月過後 , 他現在用a1醬汁吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	今天用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景已經在我們身上了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	我們所有人的意思是 , 在這房間裡的每個人可以多活五年、十年、二十年 , 僅僅因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想想人類在地球上的足跡 , 否則我們能維持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來培養新的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 及其他高度包容旱災、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植和飲食基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一的選擇 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人想自願停止飲食嗎 ?

this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一個打字機 , 數十年來 , 每個書桌的主軸 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者基因組的應用會蓬勃發展 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫展示了他的骨髓採集的一種新裝置 , 能快速收集最少痛苦的骨髓 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成年幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多末期疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物、生物科技、健康照護、醫療、醫學、科學、科技、科技 。
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一種更好的方法來收集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一位小兒科癌醫生 , 也是史丹佛大學的研究員 , 我的臨床研究重心是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感來源 , 我沒有帶給人腦 , 但我帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 他們大多有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 及其他一些疾病 。

i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國各地 , 拯救了白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.研究團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊走過 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	包柏在桌上 , 我們拿這根小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上是把這個針穿過軟組織 , 打到硬骨上 , 輸入tuchus , 每次用針筒吸取大約十mm的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它傳給護士 。 她把它注射到一個錫罐裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們不斷重覆這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後我的手臂變成索爾 , 我手上接到了一通電話 , 更不用說巴布 , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這種手術在大約40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方式來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一種減少侵入的方法 , 一種新的裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	骨髓採取器就是這裡展示的樣子
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準透明病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其輸入骨頭數十次 , 我們只輸入一次 , 進入臀部或臀部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有電力的導管 , 有一個特殊的電線尖端 , 會留在骨髓的脆弱部分 , 跟著骨盆的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你很快地渴望或吸出豐富的骨髓很快地穿過一個洞
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同一個入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能拿到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 作為門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 在史丹佛得到了一些小補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	隨之而來的是 ,
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終我們有兩隻大型動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 還得到了從骨髓採取骨髓的幹細胞活動的十倍 , 相較於正常的設備 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被美國食品及藥物管理局核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活生生生的病患 , 你可以看到它沿著彈性的曲線移動 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 在同一個洞裡 , 會有兩次通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉中進行的 , 作為門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們的幹細胞數量比同一個病人用的標準方法多了三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那你為什麼要關心呢 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗中 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們的全身包括在骨髓裡的血液變形幹細胞我們已經使用這種幹細胞療法40年了
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 使用骨髓幹細胞來治療患者的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經學治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 今年正在宣傳 , 第2.0世代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為可能救人的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年幼時就更健康 , 在未來你需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們骨髓移植者的照片 , 他們每年都會聚集在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者莉西提出了一個爭議性的宇宙模型 , 它也許能回答所有這些大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是你所見過最美妙的8d模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi認為所有事情的理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	老兄 , 看看這些殺手方程式 , 甜點 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能描述粒子物理的美麗 , 不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗和特別的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一塊珊瑚的頭都由幾千個珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚不斷地繁殖和分裂 , 成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們能想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能找到一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的位置與他的鄰居相比 , 他到底是如何處在這個特定的位置 , 和他的命運相比 , 還是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們把溫度調高太高之後 , 他告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚很可能是說 , 你看 , 我衝浪時的疤痕就證明了這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個珊瑚繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯地複製了他 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他地方也一樣 , 但卻是以獨立個體的身分體驗 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會特別準備好要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學最初是由薛丁格和他的貓所描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置中 , 薛丁格是一個放射性樣本的箱子 , 由量子力學定律 , 將它放射到一個狀態中 , 一個沒有狀態的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射線的樹枝中 , 它會啟動刺激 , 釋放毒藥 , 薛丁格死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都會經歷不同的現實 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	不管怎樣 , 另一個都不會存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很怪 , 因為我們每個人只會經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們沒有看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格這裡 , 是珊瑚分支成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是世界在微小尺度下的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都做得到 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理的其他部分則是描述能發生什麼、不能解釋什麼 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都歸結為幾何以及基本粒子的交互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動完全平衡時 , 事情才會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將向各位描述我們對這些粒子的了解它們是什麼以及這個平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速接近光速 , 聚集在一起產生一股巨大的純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子噴霧 , 探測器和電腦會找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--在日內瓦cerncerncern的cern有17英里的圓周長 , 當它在運作的時候 , 比蒙特雷市的電力要大上五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有的可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學確實告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量都必須有相同的質子和反質子的能量 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這限制更強大的粒子都不會產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它的能量極限會超出過去的七倍 , 所以我們很快就會看到新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個動物園的亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部份人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的各位 , 許多人都能過著不錯的生活來推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也是一個中性伴侶 , 叫做 「 中子 」 , 沒有電荷 , 質量很小 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下的夸克有很大的質量 , 將三者結合成為原子裡的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都分成左旋和右旋 , 有反粒子的伴侶帶著相反的電荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 電荷和第一代相同 , 但質量更高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和各種力子產生交互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過稱為光子的粒子互相作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力叫做弱力 , 只與左撇子相互作用的力 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用一種不同的載荷稱為顏色充電三種不同的品種紅、綠和藍
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann的名字他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力的力量 , 通過質量和旋轉 , 與物質產生交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	要了解這一點 , 最重要的是每一種力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力相互作用 , 根據每個粒子的載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給予所有其他粒子質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定它會成功 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性 , 關於這場演說的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們不同的旋轉和載荷來計算所有不同的粒子 , 總共有226顆 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	可以追蹤到很多粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子 , 似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據指控把它們畫出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 一個負電荷 , 而夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合在一起製造一個質子時 , 它會產生一個完整的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 有相反的電荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	原來電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷相互作用產生這種模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 電弱統一模型 」 , 它在1967年組合在一起 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們多數人只熟悉電荷而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有一個很大的質量 , 並且打破了這個電弱圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力非常弱 , 讓弱子質量很大 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯坐落在水平方向圖上 , 電磁體的光子仍然是無質量的 , 並與電荷的垂直方向互動 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以 , 電磁力和弱力是在二維空間中用這種粒子載荷模式來描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力向外擴散 , 把兩個載荷方向給標記出來 , 把載力粒子沿著這些方向畫出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以被標記在四度空間中 , 然後投影到二度空間 , 這樣我們才能看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用大自然在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞 , 它會產生能量 , 四個載荷方向的總載荷為零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 且能維持完全零電荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱子可能會腐爛成一個電子和一個反微中子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持著完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以 , 這些載荷的模式不僅漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是可以發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這樣就有一個很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強相互作用中 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個 , 與有色夸克相互作用 , 例如這個綠夸克 , 給夸克一個有不同顏色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘發生數百萬次在我們體內的每一個原子將原子核結合在一起
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但相對之下 , 這四種載荷並非故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再納入兩個載荷 , 來對應重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們放入 , 每一個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都會分開 , 在六度載荷空間中提供一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中轉動這個圖案 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們對於大自然如何在這些微小粒子的最小知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們已知的事實 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在實驗中是極限的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙處理這些微小尺度的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談一些我們還不知道的新想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單靠數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看能不能把我們的手伸展到整個enchilada身上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到組成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 當實驗到達更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這種不對稱的載荷模式 , 可以從更完美的圖案中產生 , 類似希格斯粒子如何打破電弱的圖案 , 來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向來介紹新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們推出一個新的方向時 , 我們可以猜測在這個方向上粒子的載荷 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中建構出標準載荷 , 成為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特殊的選擇 , 與1973年由pati和salam推出的偉大統一理論相對應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些空隙 , 粒子似乎不見了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的原理 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包括已成型的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 該粒子的作用應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這些載荷 , 並思考一個關於粒子的奇怪事實:物質的第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非由六個載荷獨一無二地辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 它們會互相疊加 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能給每個粒子分配出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代 , 由一種稱為 「 三重性 」 的對稱性 , 與第一代有關 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	八度空間中這種特殊的載荷模式實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大的特殊謊言群體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是一個平滑、曲線的形狀 , 有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中的曲線空間時 , 用來解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最微小的尺度運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種八度載荷空間的形狀的圖案極其美麗它總結了上千種基本粒子之間的可能互動每一種都只是這個複雜的形狀的一面
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過特定的旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿著對稱軸向下觀察這個圖案同時觀察所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 那裡的新粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個空隙其中有兩顆是patisalam粒子所填補的
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案中的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的稀有空間 , 但帶有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 讓我們得到完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	很多人認為它是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美學天體可以用想像力描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	自然界對數學的描述完全不是新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的書 , 持續對我們的目光敞開 , 用數學的語言來寫 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 若沒有這些 , 人類就無法理解單一字眼 ; 若沒有這些字 , 就會漫遊在黑暗的迷宮中 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我試著遵循伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學性
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家一起研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 數學把我們的宇宙描述成生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地方以各種不同的方式互動 , 根據美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	當使用像大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器 , 更多的圖案出現時 , 我們或許能看到大自然使用e8圖案還是不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項探索過程是一項很棒的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現新的粒子 , 但不符合這個圖案 , 那就很有趣 , 但不符合e8理論 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人也不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還蠻糟的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然的運作方式是個很危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是很長的一幕 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部分這些點子可能最後不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的野外 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資 , 在不成功的情況下 , 情緒上很難放棄一連串的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果沒有用 , 就得要丟掉它 , 嘗試其他的東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要維持理智並在不確定中獲得幸福 , 唯一的方法就是維持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能地過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪中找到平衡 , 我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 即使我工作的物理學無所不在 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年間 , 我都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母最大的謎團之一 , 我如何在不涉足全職工作的情況下 , 一直活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租 , 讓我有時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的存在有時是很困難的 , 但它讓我可以生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持生活的平衡 , 讓我很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的陪伴 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能理解其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 至少有幾個人感到興奮的原因是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它能把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是在說 , 我們應該去思考宇宙 , 它的核心 , 最小的東西 , 是e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 有沒有一個尺度 , 最小的尺度 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	亨利:現在 , 我給你們看的圖案與我們所知的基本粒子物理相對應的形狀非常美麗 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀與e8有很大的相似性 , 它與e8有很大的相似性 , 而它與e8的相似性 , 可能是這張圖的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表了高維物體的對稱性 , 它們會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有這些基本粒子的存在 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但我知道 , 弦理論家會用較小的弦振動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待一個電子與e8有關 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不 , 它會是e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以當它的形狀在時空中移動時它會扭轉 。 當它移動時扭轉的方向就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以它會是...克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它比較大嗎 ? 它比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	亨利:就我們所知的電子是 「 點粒子 」 , 這會降到最小的可能性 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性同時在擴展和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚來比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8就成了一個形狀 , 在時空中每一點都安裝在一個形狀上 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如同我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲的方式 , 會隨著它在曲面上移動 , 扭曲的形狀 , 就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 它們以此形式呈現 , 以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能說得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這無關緊要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它能激發出一種奇妙的感覺 , 我肯定想更深入地了解它 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你們來到這裡 。 這真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳說中的黑猩猩 , 珍•古德爾曾說過塔卡爾和其它社區計畫 , 協助非洲的人們和受威脅的動物住在旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學等 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德協助人類和動物生活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以 , 彈奏聲 , 彈奏聲 , 彈奏聲 , 但我們也可以oh , oooh , oooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , oooh , oooh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所打的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一個洞穴 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今晚想從昨天zeray離開的地方開始演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的三歲澳洲小孩selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽說人類的歷史、家族樹 , 經由基因側寫而成的 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 已故路易斯.李基 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時的情況很特別 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在這已經很常見了 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從這些化石中知道很多關於這些生物從化石中、從肌肉的形狀上看出它們是如何生活的從各種人造物中找到它們
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他認為現在這是一個相當常見的理論如果我們發現在我們最接近的活生生親戚身上的行為模式 , 大猩猩 , 現今的人類 , 也許這些行為是在七百萬年前出現的像猿人一樣的人類祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從那古老、古老的過去 , 帶著那些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	如果你看看現今用來處理人類演化的教科書 , 你就會發現人們會根據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比任何其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted會議中我們也聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我仍然認為 , 黑猩猩和我們是如此相似 , 在某些方面 , 牠們的行為仍然是如此 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部份的人不會在野外活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	wurzel先生 。 雌螢火蟲在11或12歲時 , 生下了第一隻寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五、六年就有一個寶寶 , 當寶寶在照顧孩子時 , 長時間的依賴感 , 晚上睡覺時 , 和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這漫長的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就跟我們一樣 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物進化過程中變得更複雜 , 我們發現學習在個人的生命歷史上扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 藉由觀察、模仿和練習 , 這種不同的在非洲黑猩猩族群中已經看到的不同的工具行為 , 這些行為是如何一代一代傳下去的 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 讓我們可以將這些工具的行為描述為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有很豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多是相似的 , 甚至相同的姿勢 , 形成相同的情境 。 歡迎給黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們還會親吻、握手、拍彼此的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會放大 , 會丟擲石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多例子都是同情心 , 愛情和真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對於他們的天性有著黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力進行極端殘暴 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分時候 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的一些人 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們是非常有侵略性的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比起其它生物 , 已經幫助我們了解到 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物之間並沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條界線非常的模糊 , 當我們觀察到更多時 , 它總是變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始進行的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外複雜的社交生活中 , 已經協助我們認識到 , 我們是其中的一部分 , 沒有被隔離的 , 是那些與我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很遺憾地發現 , 全世界許多其他生物 , 黑猩猩都在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張空氣拍攝的照片 , 它讓你看到了岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	直到大約16年前 , 我飛過了整個區域 , 才明白 , 公園以外的這片森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林在坦班尼加湖的東岸幾乎沒有被破壞 , 那裡的小小三十平方英呎的岡貝國家公園就在那裡 , 有一個問題來到我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人在掙扎求生時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地 , 更多人可能得到支援 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數量從蒲隆地湧入 , 再到剛果湖邊的湖邊 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們無法從其他地方購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致一個計畫 , 我們稱它為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種整體的方式 , 來改善住在公園附近村莊的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從十二個村莊開始 , 現在已經二十四歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探究 , 但包含像是樹木的護士之類的 , 目前最適合這種農業的方法 , 在這些山上 , 幾乎像是沙漠般的土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 這麼一來 , 就能在兩年內再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民從井裡獲得乾淨的水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和少數女性合作 , 提供她們微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 大約有95%的貸款都回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權女性與教育工作提供女孩子的獎學金讓她們能完成中學的學業在全世界都明白女性的教育改善家庭的規模下降
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 有些事情發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育發生的是住在24個村落的農夫 , 不是看著我們 , 而是一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 坦尚尼亞的許多員工現在是坦尚尼亞的 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞的團隊進入了村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民交談 , 問他們感興趣什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求有更多的了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白山坡上層被砍伐了 , 所以土壤流失和泥石流很嚴重 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的更大的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠離國家公園 , 延伸到這些被破壞的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的土地放到一邊 , 所以 , 同樣的 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩也會有葉子走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園以外的遺傳性交流 , 與其它遺傳性的團體交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以坦尚尼亞造林計劃是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們將它複製於非洲的其他區域 , 其它野生地區面臨著極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲的問題 , 正如我們在過去這前幾天一直在討論的 , 是很大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有相當多的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的人生活在沒有肥料的土地上 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 讓土壤向外開放 , 因為絕望的族群砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 所以他們可以試著種植食物給自己和家人 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要給錢 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	除了非洲之外 , 還有其他的問題 , 還有其他的發展中國家 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了些什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華威爾森曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人的平均生活水準是歐洲人或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的地球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說的是四種 , 但我們沒有它們 , 我們有一顆 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 這裡是最聰明的人 , 可以走遍地球 , 擁有這種非凡的大腦 , 能夠用這些ted研討會所描繪出的科技 , 而我們卻摧毀了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 通常會坐下來問自己: 「 這樣的決定會如何影響我們前七代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定──我在這裡不特別談非洲 , 但已開發國家的重大決定 , 涉及數百萬美金 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一次股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響到非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我越來越了解到有多少非洲的問題會留在過去殖民時期的門口 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到外面的非洲旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們都知道我在說什麼 。 我在說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是本世紀最關鍵的議題之一 , 水資源在各地被污染 , 被農業、工業、家庭的化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質在全世界仍然被噴灑著 , 看似沒有辦法從過去的經驗中獲益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 像海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不計代價地燃燒石化燃料 , 還有其他的溫室氣體 , 所謂的 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人都開始相信我們的氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混雜在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人受到更嚴重的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	是已經被影響的非洲 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉沙漠以南的非洲 , 乾旱更加嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 通常會造成洪水和災難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在無法支援的地區 , 貧窮的人無法購買食物 , 他們無法搬走 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 隨著最後一棵樹木被砍伐 , 沙漠化 , 令人毛骨悚然 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這種超聰明的大腦和ted科技所顯現出來的人類心智可能有某種隔閡嗎 ? 用非科學的方法來說 , 用愛和同理心來談論它 。 是否有某種隔閡 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是沮喪或冷漠的 , 或是苦惱和憤怒的 。 他們說的幾乎是一樣的: 「 我們覺得這是因為我們覺得你已經折磨了我們的未來 , 我們對未來也無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 我想我們從小就已經傷害了這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這導致我們稱之為 「 根與芽 」 的計畫 , 始於坦尚尼亞 , 目前已擴展到全球97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根是堅固的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 ; 要抵達太陽 , 他們就可以穿過一道磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為是我們在地球上所遭受的所有問題環境和社會問題 , 它是一種希望的訊息
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界數以百計的年輕人可以突破 , 讓這個世界變得更好 , 讓所有生物都能活得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的信息:我們每一個人 , 都能造成不同 , 每天都如此 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在這房間裡的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 來決定我們想要做什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人別無選擇 。 由我們決定改變現狀 , 窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體會選擇三個專案 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於它們的年齡 , 不管在哪個國家 , 不管是在城市還是鄉村 , 不管是哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在已經從幼稚園到大學 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們的根部及芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇三個不同的專案讓這個世界變得更好 , 認識到所有這些不同的問題都息息相關 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能做到 , 他們就能籌集資金 , 協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個計畫是幫助動物不僅是野生動物 , 家庭動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	整體來說 , 要學習和平和諧、和諧、我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、宗教之間、和大自然之間的和平共存 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能以我們速度毀滅它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	僅僅從非洲的一兩個項目中挑選出來 , 根與芽的群體 , 在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果的烏干達、剛果、獅子山、喀麥隆 , 及其它團體 。 如我所說的 , 全世界有97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種植樹木 , 他們在種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 賣雞蛋 , 賣一些錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽家人 , 感覺到一種驕傲和賦權感 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依賴別人種植蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予士兵一些心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	像這樣的專案計畫 , 讓它們自己脫身 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再次強調 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以現在根本就沒有更多的根與芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要成份 , 讓年長的孩子和年長的孩子交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不希望懷孕之類的 , 讓年輕人傾聽其他青年 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地被問到的問題是: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看到你的黑猩猩從一百萬隻到現在已經數量減少 , 沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他的動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經是森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚訝的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	想想看科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我真的很興奮 , 終於 , 來到大家談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的其中一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水都沖到水底下 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談論再生能源 , 非常重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心我們孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以為此做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活做點什麼 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼、穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不論是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心臟結合在一起 , 我們在世界各地聯手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted協助我們做得很好的 , google也幫了我們 , esri也幫我們繪製了岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今天下午已經聽說過了 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這個改變 , 這個改變 。 如果我們在乎未來 , 我們必須要看到我們必須要改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	大自然的下一個希望的理由是令人驚訝的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以在一個完全被摧毀的區域中 , 利用時間 , 或許有一些可以讓它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你們 , 一個看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止砍柴 , 那你就不需要去了 , 因為你有木材 , 那五年後 , 你就可以有30呎長的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎絕種的邊緣 , 可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它激勵了我 。 它也帶到了我最後一類的希望 , 在過去的兩天裡 , 我們聽過這麼多關於這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人們的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 使得那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 有時 , 可以親自去幫助他們 , 帶著他們的一份心去改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看非洲有一兩人真的很鼓舞人心 。
