instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是身體活動、保齡球、打曲棍球、自行車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但不吃太多 , 他們吃的沒錯 , 他們很投入 , 且很值得信任和值得信任 , 隨時間推移 , 就會產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食可以供應超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常一月開始 , 通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	至於長壽 , 藥丸或其他任何東西都沒有短期補助 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想一想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做最重要的事情 , 可以在生命中加上更多年 。 年復一年 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	傳導電氣的墨水 ; 一扇窗戶 , 從明顯變換到不透明 ; 一個可以產生音樂的水母 。 所有的這些東西都存在 。 催產素mota說:該是玩的時候了 。 mota帶領我們參觀令人驚訝又酷的新材料 , 並暗示我們怎樣去找出它們的好處 , 去實驗、修改它 , 並享受它的樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智慧型材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有個朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機打造一台車 , 讓他可以運送家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他之所以這麼做 , 是因為他買不起車 , 也是因為他知道如何建造車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 如何製造和修理 , 或至少知道要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀後半葉 , 許多這些做法都被遺失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社群和開放原始碼的模式正將這些知識帶回我們的生活中 , 了解事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是什麼組成的 。 我相信我們需要提升它們的下一個階段 , 到形成的組成階段 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道傳統的紙和紡織品是什麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人、未來化的複合材料 , 會改變形狀、會導電的顏料、會改變顏色的顏料、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電油墨讓我們不用傳統印刷電路或電線來塗鴉電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上拿著這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 它會對我的皮膚做出反應 , 打開這個小光 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨被藝術家使用過 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就會在雷射印表機和筆中使用它 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一片水晶體 , 裡面佈滿了無色光源的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的水晶只會在邊緣散發光線 , 當我打開光線時 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	已知兩種這種材料的應用包括室內設計以及多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱電顏料在特定溫度下會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我要把這個放到熱板上 , 只放到比環境溫度稍高一點點 , 各位可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這項材料的主要應用在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它能指示內容物是否涼爽到可以飲用 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般所知的智慧型材料中的一小部分 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會被我們每天使用的物品和科技給影響 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法將那些會飛的汽車科幻小說給我們保證 , 但是我們可以用溫度改變顏色的牆壁 , 鍵盤會捲起來 , 窗戶會變得不透明 , 在開關的瞬間 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一位社會科學家 , 為什麼我要來這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何形成的 , 還有它們是如何形成的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入地了解組成我們世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的複合物的了解不夠多 , 我們的未來會是由這些組成的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在少量下取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 很少人知道它們是如何被製造出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	目前為止 , 它們大多存在這個貿易秘密和專利領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我和kirsty男孩開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放式材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發佈資訊 , 鼓勵大家隨時都能貢獻 , 把資源聚集起來 , 比如其他像我們一樣的自造者的研究論文和課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體產生的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料來提供自身資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料如何運作 , 以及它們的組成 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們不了解、不使用的東西 , 最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿著的衣服、住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要了解並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由小提琴手推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學很複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們發表論文時 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦•布朗克在讀到這篇論文後 , 完全沒有化學經驗 , 並在他的自造者空間中繁殖實驗 , 只靠現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用了烤箱做成自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一位科學家的指導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦後來將結果發表在網路上 , 包括他嘗試過、不成功的所有結果 , 讓其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的創新形式是把一個實驗放在設備良好的大學實驗室裡 , 在芝加哥的車庫裡 , 用他自己製作的便宜材料和工具 , 來重現它 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項研究 , 其他人可以在他離開的地方想出更簡單的程序 , 並改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想要提及她的專案目標的例子是強調材料的品質同時著重在建構者的創意和技能
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子採集包非常強大 , 它們能教導我們事情是如何運作的 , 但設計中固有的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面漢娜的辦法是制定一系列的技術來創造出不尋常的物體透過教導我們認識材料本身
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗中這是我最喜歡的實驗之一
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有銅線和mp3播放器和磁鐵連接
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工科羅的研究漢娜用各式各樣的材料製作了一系列的紙喇叭從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布及墨水
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造家漢娜出版了自己的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製和繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最理想的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜、靈活的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝品 , 以及她共享的發現 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 無論是美學還是創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的地方在於我們創造了熱情和好奇心 , 而我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不規則的角度來處理問題 , 過程中 , 我們發現了替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究者就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造者他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得我有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定要了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主機 , 沒有人夢想著在家裡有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在一定要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 收集新興科技的先發知識是確保我們能在未來發聲的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入一個玻璃泡泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠我們的眼睛來引導我們儘管我們只能看到前方的幾輛車 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 關於它們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路徑 ? 珍妮佛依然能想像一個世界沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車子能說話 , 意外事故可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教的圖標和好運的圖標出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16到19歲死因的主要原因 , 車禍是造成死亡的主因 , 百分之七十五的車禍和毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是一位年輕的駕駛在高速公路上 , 在我面前的車輛 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也要慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停了下來 , 停了下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs踢了進來 , 車仍然向前駛 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停止 , 空氣袋子的部署 , 車子全部完整了 , 很幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子在停 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想 , 我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓你們稍微想想現在的駕駛經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃的氣泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是用分散式路徑來導航 , 在其他的金屬巨人身上 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只要指導你就是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的眼睛不是設計來完成這項任務的 , 但人們會問你 , 像是 , 你想要做些改變 , 他們問你的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上移開 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看著你要去哪裡 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不去看路邊的路 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做呢 ? 因為我們必須必須選擇我要看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們都在做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得不對勁或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數次的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來臨了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技能協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車交換資料 , 我們不只能看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛視野 , 我們還能看到車子內的車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看前面的車子走得多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要去零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 , 有車子 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路上行駛 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在已出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理的預測 , 並不難預測在不遠的未來汽車會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使你在車子裡 , 車子裡有摩托車騎士來了 , 時速85英哩 , 車道降低了 , 我知道你有種經驗 , 那個人並不是 「 無所不在 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	這傢伙可能已經走過了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	沒錯吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英哩前 , 有人看到那個人 , 當一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放到地圖上時 , 他就在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會以85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他耳邊低語 , 像是: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘後 , 機車會小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這點很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 像是分享我們車子的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車上有gps和照相機 , 我就會很精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我就可以估算我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 以及車子要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己在哪裡 , 並且有點模糊地說出車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享這些數據 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃wang教授和他的團隊做了一些電腦模擬 , 來估計當混合物的結果 , 即便是輕軌的交通量 , 當車只是分享gps資料時 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移出 , 移入了實際的感測器 , 裝在這些機器人上 , 像是立體攝影機、gps , 以及二維雷射測量器 , 這些都是很常見的後備系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還安裝了短距的無線電 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人靠近彼此時 , 它們能精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你講太多話題時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 而這就是預測模型能幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會那麼注意那些軌跡 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離軌道的人排在第一位 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離軌道 , 你知道怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道你需要警告哪些駕駛 , 才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想怎麼能警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼能輕聲疾呼: 「 你需要走出去嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做點什麼 , 他們就不會站在緊急狀況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做一系列的 「 駕駛州立模式 」 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測出一個駕駛向前看、往下看、手機上看、或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外狀況 , 我們可以預測誰是車子 , 哪些車子最好離路線 , 來為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技現在就存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面對的最大問題是我們自願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個非常令人不安的想法 , 我們的車子會監視我們 , 和其他車子談 , 我們會在流言的大海上走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種保護我們的隱私的方式 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我真的不知道你是怎麼做的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的車牌號碼 , 我不會知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不希望被分散的青少年留在你身後 , 知道你在煞車 , 知道你正要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做到最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車閒聊著你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現他進入太空的夢想 , 透過飛行到上層大氣層 , 體驗到0g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、飛行、科學、短談、太空、科技、宇宙 ,
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的 「 0gg 」 中 , 彼得•戴曼迪斯 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我有多熱衷於打開太空的領域 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以 , 當我有機會給予世界重力專家無重力的體驗時 , 真的很不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是基因體的archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 給第一組在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 基因體一百個人 」 , 我們將它定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特是那個事件的主席 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想就是到太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我能帶你進入無重力狀態 , 進入無重力狀態 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要體驗地球上唯一的零度 , 其實只有拋物線飛行 , 沒有重量飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭乘一架飛機 , 飛到頂部 , 你是無重力的 , 飛了25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回到下面 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再、再、再、再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 讓美國太空總署長久以來都在訓練太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府部門和一間飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場記者會 , 我們宣佈了我們想要做一個無重力拋物線飛行器 , 給他25秒的0 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果進行得非常好 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行器 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他會想去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著被災難摧毀的風險 ,
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想要鼓勵大眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的車內 , 來到零號飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募集了15萬美金的捐款給兒童慈善機構他們與我們一起飛 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室的醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們設置了一切以緊急情況為例 , 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭降落的地方 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和夥伴bonlichtenberg小心地將他吊死為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他抵達那裡 , 我們就讓他體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線飛行過後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 , 他在微笑 , 我們就走了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行器 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上把一顆蘋果以致敬艾薩克•牛頓爵士因為霍金教授在劍橋舉著和牛頓一樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	再來是第七、第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們要離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入這場史詩般的冒險旅程 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師大衛•布林斯基有3分鐘的驚人動畫展現了細胞內的充斥生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一個醫學插圖師 , 我的觀點有點不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察 , 藝術中真與美的表達方式 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	這些都是他們自己的美好事物 , 他們都有非常美好的事物 , 可以把科學和數學看成理想 , 可以被科學和數學看成是理想的雙胞胎 , 就像是科學家想要去約會的理想連接雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真理是令人敬畏的 , 意思是 , 它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是理想的、有力的、不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時很有用 , 通常是在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你們可以放一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美是常常不可忽視的 , 那些不在科學領域的人 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是描述美的事物 , 通常只有當你了解它的語言和它所研究的主題時 , 才能夠接觸到它 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有人類學的理想 , 你看到生命從描述宇宙的數字中進化 , 這些是非常難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當醫學插圖師以來我被教導動畫和視覺輔導我想要找出一種方法來幫助人們了解生物科學用動畫、圖片、故事 , 以至於我被教導讓人們了解真相和美這對人們來說是不必要的
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常沉浸在一個環境中 , 在這裡 , 他們所學到的主題是真與美 , 但他們被教導的方式是分割式的 , 並且被縮減到一個不見得都是事實和美麗的主題 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	像是雞湯的老食譜 , 把雞肉煮熟 , 直到香味消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子和細胞生物學系的robertlue打來的電話 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真的改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一個計畫 , 來探索細胞 , 來探索在分子和細胞生物學中的真和美 , 如此一來 , 學生就能了解一個更大的圖片 , 可以把這些事實掛在身上 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能會對細胞產生一種心理印象 , 像是一個大型、破壞、巨大的複雜城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地奈米專家的忌妒 , 它們都是自我導向、強大、準確的裝置 , 它們是由一串胺基酸組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械能驅動細胞運作的方式 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製的方式 。 它們能驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是想出如何把這個故事做成動畫 , 讓它成為哈佛生物分裂的中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子和細胞生物分裂學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文本資料 , 除了這些文字內容之外 , 讓學生能以視覺化的方式呈現 , 這樣這些學生就能內化細胞的真與美 , 並且能夠研究它們的想像力 , 如此一來 , 他們就能被激發 , 去發現它們的新生命 , 如此一來 , 它們就能夠被激發 , 去發現它們的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 巨噬細胞在微血管下流動 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會接收來自微血管細胞的資訊 , 這些細胞在微血管壁上 , 它們會被送到外面某處有發炎狀態的資訊 , 在那裡 , 它們看不見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會使他們停止 , 使他們內化 , 他們需要做出所有會讓他們改變形狀的各個部分 , 並試著離開這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們和哈佛大學的科學家及資料庫模型一起合作 , 研究原子上精確的分子 , 找出它們的動作 , 找出它們的動作 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法用真誠的方式來做這件事 , 來改善正在發生的狀況 , 但在牢房中投入的人群 , 並沒有那麼誠實 , 能阻止這個景象發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要介紹一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本我們製作的這個影片的最初版本 。 這是一個正在進行的專案計畫 , 將會持續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這張圖 , 看看細胞製造這些步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為驅動蛋白 , 負責大小相對的大量載重物 。
run the movie , please .	請播放影片 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此之間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會導致細胞內不同的事發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會利用讀取基因的分子來製造它需要的零件 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的所有人 , 如果沒有這些微機械 , 生命就有可能發生 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率會非常大 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他拉著一袋滿是新製造的蛋白質到細胞所需要的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不論是到一個器官 , 不論是用來製造或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人身上都有大約十萬個這種東西在你一百兆個細胞內跑來跑去 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你覺得有多懶惰 , 本質上你什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 回家後 , 我希望你能想想 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看我們正在學習的細胞機制 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了所有正在發生的事 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎都知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞懂了發生什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌握大量掌控我們的健康 , 用我們未來的世代 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們知道細胞需要什麼樣的特性 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起合作 , 讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起合作 , 協助我們身體的巨大團體 , 讓它們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓打算在她的車裡住一整年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症發生 , 她的露營之旅就結束了 , 在這個親密的演說中 , 她描述了成為一個美國無家可歸者的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險 , 快樂 , 生活 , 個人成長 , 貧窮 , 社會改變 , 說故事 , 說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:我無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家 , 也是記者 , 我也是個非常好奇的人 , 所以身為記者 , 我學會了很多新的東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了無家者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作 , 就在我父親同年二月去世後 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我相當難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 我有很多想要感受和處理的東西 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定住在一輛旅行車上一年 , 要這樣做 , 大概是一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了貓、旋轉器和營地裝備 , 打進了一輛1975年雪佛蘭旅車 , 開車出門到日落 , 我完全沒意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會把 「 固定 」 的結構 , 甚至一堆 「 價值觀 」 等同於 「 人 」 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒辦法很快地體會到 , 別人的負面看法對我們的現實有多大的影響 , 如果我們放手 ,
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 。 我定期的吃完飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 父親過世的憤怒和沮喪就開始了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的工作就這樣結束了 。 我必須找一份全職的工作來支付這些帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	真正溫和的春天變成了非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到處都是公園 , 完全看不出來我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓進來 , 穿過了車窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗照顧狗狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	無論何時 , 我都在辦公大樓的員工洗澡和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者 , 我在公共餐廳洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓車子很難或無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱能中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰層 , 幾個小時內就融化了 , 情況非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法找到一間公寓 , 或無法負擔得起一間公寓 , 讓我能擁有老貓和老貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣讓我太厲害 , 無法再走50英尺路到我車外的公共廁所時 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度降到冰點以下 , 氣溫就會降到這裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一大堆新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都會在不同的地方停車 , 這樣我就不會被警察察察察察察察察察發現並逮捕 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時、如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 轉變為一個無家者 , 住在一輛車上 , 深呼吸了我 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 。 我的智商沒掉下來 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的誠信、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切 , 都仍然是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但不知怎麼的 , 我改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在憂鬱症中越深處越深處 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提到我去無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我已經三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中任何人一樣臭、沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家者發現 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 。 你為什麼來到這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者並沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我真的認為我是無家可歸的 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有一份工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥效讓我自殺了 。 我記得當時心想: 「 如果我自殺了 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯特 , 一位全國知名記者 , 一直在對我講國家電視節目 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在演說電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆羅斯 , 《與媒體見面》的前主持人 , 談到我的寫作 , 當時我住在一輛沃爾瑪停車場的貨車上 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為我到達了那個時候 , 我是一個作家 , 還是我是個無家者 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀書 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車上 , 和沙發上衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏得獎項的 , 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再被隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續被汙名化 , 把住在你車輛或街道上的罪犯化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者 , 勞動無家者 , 主要還是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服一切 , 只要它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的女生 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個你遇見的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人並不是他們住的地方 , 也不是他們睡哪裡 , 也不是他們任何時候的生活狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在沃爾瑪超市的貨車上 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠 , 總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 " 保險套 " , 墨西維拉瓦迪亞帶領我們走遍全國的大膽計劃 , 從1970年代開始 , 從人口控制的第一步 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 奇怪 , 非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學等 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	墨西維拉瓦迪亞:保險套如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有許多許多人生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利方案開始 , 也不是貧窮減少方案 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃計劃開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕育兒童健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:要去兒童 , 去找媽媽 , 然後跟著家計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會開藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不 」 視為一個答案 ; 我們把 「 不 」 視為一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找同樣是女性的護士和助產士 , 向她們解釋如何使用藥丸是很棒的 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它只覆蓋了全國20%的人口 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	對於剩下80%的人 , 我們該怎麼做 ? 告訴他們: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找了普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色的標誌下 , 我真希望他們沒有消失 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選擇的對象是我們的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道客戶永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己會練習家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應避孕藥和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 就這樣 , 我們去找那些被視為問題的起因的人 , 去做解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論人們在哪裡 , 都會看到女人在賣東西 , 這裡是漂浮市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶把聖水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 給家人聖潔 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳遍全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村落的僧人自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它是被祝福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何東西 , 讓人類更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母來規劃家庭計畫-a、b代表、c代表保險套、iud、v代表腸切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們拿到蛇和梯子遊戲 , 把骰子丟掉 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何平凡的規劃上著陸 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 母親 。 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 很好 , 叔叔 。 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	舅舅喝醉了 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再來一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育、階級娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做同樣的事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有接力賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套就被視為是女孩的最佳朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說鑽石不是唯一的安全套所以保險套是女孩的最佳朋友
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 而組織的婦女說: 「 我們只想借錢給實踐家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你就可以向我們借錢 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是靠他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年之後 , 仍然持續著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是基金 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個龐大的組織來運作它是由村民自己來運作的 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能根本不會看到泰國人 , 那裡總是女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們就認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供輸精管切除手術 , 特別是 , 美國男性排隊前面 , 排到大使館的住院 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們球場 , 給了我們非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然是午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物不是漢堡就是熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是一位年輕人 , 名叫威利•博姆 , 他為美國國際援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯 , 他接受剖腹手術是因為他的熱狗一半被吃掉 , 而且他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國傳播了很多新聞 , 有些人也很憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 來吧 , 我會全部的人來做 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切中 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3%到0.5% 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以說它是可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡的話 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂跟著我們還是可口可樂但我們是好朋友
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是所有人加入的情況 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強勢的政府 。 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都可以改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病襲擊泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	我心想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 就去軍事那裡 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去找軍方 , 請求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們的槍比政府多 , 他們的槍比政府多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否幫助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計資料之後 , 他們說: 「 好的 。 你可以使用所有的電台 , 電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們就開始使用飛機 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	不久之後 , 我們接到了新的總理 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 mechai , 你可以加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他詢問我是因為他很喜歡我太太 。
so i said , " okay . "	我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 增加預算的五十倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至是法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病的教育 , 每一個人 , 我們都說公眾、機構、宗教機構、學校 , 所有人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	而在這裡 , 每一個媒體人都必須接受愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每一站50分鐘額外的廣告額外收入更多的錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此很滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校都有愛滋病的教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生 , 正在教高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女孩 , 不是男孩 , 她們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些到處教導安全性愛和愛滋病毒的女孩們 , 被稱為泰瑞莎修女 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再往下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級的孩子 , 四年級 , 去村子裡的每個家庭 , 全泰國的家庭 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每一個家庭 , 給這些小孩子們 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有任何家長反對 , 因為我們想要拯救生命 , 這是個救生員 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	公司也知道生病的員工不管用 , 消費者也不買東西 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都受過訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們拿著他的哈佛大學mba學院的保險套到學校和夜店
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 , 你需要一些東西的象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每一個方案 , 你都需要一個符號 , 而這可能是他與mba的最佳成就 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們把保險套送到街道各處 , 到處都是 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	計程車上有保險套 。
and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	同時 , 在交通事故中 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察和橡膠 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	你們能想像一下 , 紐約警察放出保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 他們會極度享受它 。 我看到他們站在那兒 , 到處都看得到 。
imagine if they had condoms , giving out to all sorts of people .	想像一下 , 如果有保險套 , 提供給各種人 。

and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們推出的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	有人說: 「 大規模防護性武器 。 」
we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現這裡有人在尋找大規模殺傷性武器 , 但我們已經找到了大規模防護性武器:保險套 。
and then it says here , with the american flag , " don't leave home without it . "	上面寫著 , 美國國旗: 「 若不留意 , 不要離開家裡 。 」
but i have some to give out afterward .	但之後我還是要放棄一些 。

and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以 , 我們說: 「 我們相信橡膠 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到 , 我們把一切加到我們的努力中 , 來讓人們的生活更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們把保險套放在飯店和學校的冰箱裡 , 因為酒精會損害判斷力 。

after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 每個人都加入了 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國的統計 , 愛滋病的新案例減少了90% , 根據世界銀行的統計 , 770萬條人命被拯救了 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有多少泰國人到處走動 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	剛剛顯示了 , 你可以做點什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	有政治的承諾 , 一些金融的承諾 , 每個人都加入這場戰爭 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	然後我們決定幫助貧窮的人 , 現在我們以這種方式讓愛滋病離開 , 不再只靠政府 , 而是和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和信譽 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些東西是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們正試著將它們轉變為赤腳企業家、小型商業人士 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法 , 就是透過企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司的資金透過樹木移植 , 流入村莊 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢投入小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們帶來了錢 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用證據應該是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用權必須是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你必須先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為赤腳mba , 教導人們如何做生意 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些事業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這些事很有趣 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該不再做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	還有泰國絲綢 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們在做蘇格蘭的標籤 , 如你所見 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先的人 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人只要坐下來看電視 , 和我聯絡 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	這是我們在泰國的星巴克回答: 「 咖啡和保險套 。 」
see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	你看 , 星巴克你醒著 , 我們讓你醒著並活著 。

you can order your condoms with your with your cappuccino .	你可以用卡布奇諾訂購保險套 。
and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	接著 , 最後 , 在教育方面 , 我們想要改變學校 , 成為每個人終身學習中心的地方 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為以學校為基礎的農村整合發展 。
and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	這是一個中心 , 一個對經濟和社會發展的焦點 。
