your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得像是朋友 , 但真朋友會給你一絲微笑 。 在2013年 , 凱勒•瑞納多示範romo , 智慧型手機操作機器人 , 可以和你一起散步 , 滑著一杯咖啡橫跨桌子 , 讓你對你做出可程控的表情反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機供電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手表示有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	你們當中不多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好 , 請舉手如果你不包含roomba的話你們家裡有多少機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive公司試圖解決的問題 , 我和romotive的二十位書呆子都著迷於解決這個問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要製造一個人人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要做出一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不只可以負擔得起 , 它還得要是人們真的想要帶回家 , 繞著他們的孩子走 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不會很詭異或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善、可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 使用你已經知道且很愛你的iphone來當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造一個可以無線上網的機器人 , 且電腦視覺辨識的150美元 , 大約是這類機器人在過去所花費的1% 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他處於創造模式 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	他其實是用這個裝置上的攝影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲開 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很謹慎 , 所以他會一直盯著我 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我過來這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我過來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其它生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己想法的寵物一樣 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--喔 ~ ~ romo累了 , 如果我想要用romo來探索世界 , 我其實可以把他和任何ios設備連結起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	romo會將視訊串流到這個裝置 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	我可以看到romo看到的一切 , 我得到機器人的視角 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是appstore的免費app軟體 , 如果在座的任何人手機上都有這個應用程式 , 我們現在就可以共享這個機器人的控制權 , 一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我會很快的給你們看 , romo實際上是在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看到我和整個ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我在這裡拿到romo 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以我可以帶他到處走 , 我可以拍你們的照片 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要有一張1500個人的ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	所以我拍了一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就如同你在ipad上滑動的內容 , 我可以調整這個裝置的鏡頭角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	通過romo的眼睛 , 你們所有人都能看見 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒來表達我自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以 , 我可以進去 , 說讓我們讓romo興奮一點 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo , 最重要的是 , 我們想要創造一個完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教導別人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰會想開機器人呢 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你不需要和機器人在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他真的會在任何兩個智慧型設備之間串流雙向的聲音和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以透過瀏覽器登入 , 有點像在輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們剛剛談到遠端臨場感 , 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 有一支iphone , 她媽媽會給她買機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 放在機器人上 , 發送電子郵件給住在美國另一邊的奶奶 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每天晚上十五分鐘 , 否則她一年只能見到她孫女一兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我想談談我們未來正在努力的事來結束我的演講 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們的一位工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在谷歌開放框架上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些程式碼 , 放下這些程式碼 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這些行為 , 就像你看到romo在左邊所做的一樣 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 , 在現實生活中執行 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你引以為傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上每一個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些有wifi功能的機器人其實彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們如此專注於建造一個人人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最有說服力的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是一百年或一百億美金 , 也不是一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它取決於像你們一樣的小型敏捷機器人 , 以及像你們一樣的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們等不及要看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活動家伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化等 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 真的很可怕 , 能來到這裏是最聰明的人之一 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真實的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比事實更真實的東西關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有的故事都吸引我 , 有些則令我煩惱 , 直到最後我寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫了巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔術 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直以匿名的生活 , 直到2006年2月 , 我帶著奧運旗在義大利冬季奧運 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在人們認可我在梅西的名人 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個籌辦奧運的籌辦人打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗手之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是誤認身分的案例 , 因為身為運動員 , 我盡可能從不被提及 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以走在體育場裡 , 不用路人 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性才會帶著奧運旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 穿著制服 , 要求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我曾在一個鬆軟的主動脈中想像過自己 , 看起來就像米其林的男人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時在街上有80個奧運團隊 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了所有的競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還是有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一小塊雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 一股風力 , 可以決定比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	海報的街道上滿是紅色海報 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動我們的動力 , 決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那就是我書中角色需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要長城長、異議者、冒險家、局外人和反抗者 , 他們問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	友善的人通常不會有有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好前夫 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他的旗手三位運動員 , 演員蘇珊珊•沙蘭和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩位有熱情的女性 , 旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	索馬利夫人 , 柬埔寨積極分子 , 積極對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 他們相信和非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒她們 , 治好愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而在被迫接收5、15個客戶的妓院中 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的衣服 , 但和米其林人裝的衣服差得遠 。 說真的 , 不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 大部分的旗幟也都一樣 , 是美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高 , 有很深的皮膚 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 要怎麼有深色的皮膚 , 卻沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談中問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好看 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不會發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡你有一些來自地球上最美麗的女性的免費建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不屈不撓 , 不咳嗽 , 不吹噓 , 不跟自己說話 , 不放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	她並沒有說得那麼清楚 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	約午夜時 , 我們被召集到體育館的翅膀 , 擴音器發出奧運旗 , 順便一提 , 音樂是從這裡開始的 , 愛達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一呎 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩膀上拿著國旗 。 我在後方跑到我的尖端手臂上拿著國旗 , 這樣我的頭其實是在該死的旗下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的相機都是在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體上 , 我也出現了 , 雖然常常出現在蘇菲雅的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都希望去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是在奧林匹克體育館裡 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我說這句話時 , 我的丈夫會被冒犯 , 雖然我向他解釋說 , 我們在私下的做法通常會花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自接受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的所有剪輯 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 老年時摧毀了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運們熱情的關鍵詞
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有個關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 剛果的圖西族難民營是一座監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女人和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為剛果的一個死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺害的人 , 會因為疾病或飢餓而死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪班多 , 以及她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產兒子 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子切割臍帶 , 用頭髮將之連結起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的名字來為雙胞胎命名 , 讓雙胞胎得益 , 並用黑茶餵食 , 因為她的母乳無法維持 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵衝進她的牢房強暴她最大的女兒時 , 她抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們抓著一把槍到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這個家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 靠著不平凡的運氣 , 和熱情的美國人sashachnofff , 他成功地把她送到美國救援機場 , 蘿絲和她的九個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑那州的鳳凰城 , 在那裡生活和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯華西里語中代表著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且富有熱情的女性 , 像是蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們組成 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性、為女性工作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很熟悉 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在一個父權的天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲時是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到達智利 , 所以沒有人知道我到底哪裡出了問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 要給我的自由付出很高的代價 , 還要向父權社會提出質疑 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為每次我被罰款 , 我都能遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女權主義已經過時了 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們打了一場記憶深刻的戰爭 。 女權主義已經過時了嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於我女兒和在座各位一樣有特權的女性 , 在世界上大部分的姊妹仍然被強迫結婚、賣淫、強迫工作 , 她們的孩子不想要或她們無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 甚至被無辜殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我保證我從來沒有停止調情 , 我很少受到男性的苦難 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義還沒死 , 絕對沒有 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的口味 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為雌激素 , 金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想得到的名字都無所謂只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 一個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這地方是孟加拉村莊的一間小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	時間是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 她在她的三週假期中當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要清潔牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間小屋 , 裡面都是蒼蠅 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一排女子等了好幾個小時接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人痛苦無盡 , 因為她有幾個壞掉的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的辦法就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有被授權 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她常常冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但幸好她帶來了一些麻醉藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有著勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她鼓起了一名禱告 , 然後開始行動 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 解脫的病人親吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生專家又拔出更多牙齒了 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在和她的丈夫等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這女人的臉看起來像個水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此腫脹 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	先生 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 接著 , 翻譯解釋說病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她先生打她 , 因為她不在家裡準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性是這樣生活的 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性分擔了三分之二的全世界勞動力 , 但她們卻擁有不到全世界1%的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男人低 , 如果他們有薪水 , 他們仍然是弱勢的 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己收入的能力、繼承和擁有財產的能力 , 給予社會福利 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女人有權力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人能繁榮 , 村落就會繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•馬塔伊去了肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談 , 告訴她們土地是貧瘠的 , 因為土地是砍伐和賣掉樹木的 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 澆水 , 再掉下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	五或六年後 , 一片森林充足了土壤 , 拯救了村莊 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最落後的社會總是那些讓女性失望的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善事業忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性專案的每一塊錢 , 可以提供二十美元給男性專案計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦權會改變一切 , 不只是科技、設計、娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性共同工作 , 連結、有知識、受過教育的女性 , 能為這星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷大部分都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 , 她們是附帶的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們這一團混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 生活品質也為每個人豐富 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月時我看到費南多•波特羅在柏克萊大學圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 帶著博特羅的作品 , 卻膽敢展示這些畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	畫作中有巨大的折磨和濫用權力畫作 , 用大量的巴特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的心中或我的心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無辜的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 並迫使其他雄性領袖接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但總是對它們有益 , 在這個例子中 , 下滲效應 , 在經濟上沒有用 , 效果完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待行為從梯子的上方滑到下方 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	尤其是貧窮的婦女和兒童 , 尤其是貧窮的婦女和兒童 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧窮的男人也有自己可以虐待女人或小孩的人
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數人透過性別、收入、種族和階級來推動運動的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是成熟的 , 可以為我們的文明做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能量來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要許多有權力的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我指的是年輕男性 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是沒有希望的 , 我們必須等著他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很希望蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇性的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要選擇 , 我寧願有顆勇敢的心臟 , 像是孟加拉、索馬利的母親、珍妮和玫瑰的地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、能源、天賦和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是被服務過的 。 但從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵 , 討論了供給城市的日常奇蹟 , 展示古老的食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳鋼鐵:食物如何形塑我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽城市的食物 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問過 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們去商店、餐廳 , 或甚至去劇院的門廳 , 在大約一個小時的時間內 , 那裡就有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處冒出來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為倫敦這麼大的城市 , 每天有足夠的食物被生產、運輸、購買、販賣、烹煮、吃、完全丟棄 , 同樣的事也發生在地球上的每一天 , 都能餵飽城市 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的地方 , 忘記了我們是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 事實上我們依賴大自然 , 就像我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人遷入城市 , 更多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 如我身後的景觀──在巴西的馬托格羅索的黃豆田 , 目的就是要餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的風景 , 但我們當中很少人見過這些景色 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這樣的景觀不僅僅是用來餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們搬到城市裡 , 更多人在吃肉 , 全球有三分之一的農作物現在被餵食給動物 , 而非我們動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物 , 才能餵飽一個人 , 如果它先通過一隻動物 , 那不是非常有效率的餵飽方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個逐步的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計到我們有兩倍的人口住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳製品的消耗量也會是兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市化是手工增長的 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	在2050年之前 , 六十億人餓著肉食性動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續下去 , 那我們就不太可能解決這個問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有110萬公頃的熱帶雨林被砍伐 , 創造出新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	同時 , 我們也失去了相當於現有的可耕地來鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方每一卡路里所消耗的食物要耗約十卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們所生產的食物很昂貴 , 但我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的一半食物已經被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有妥善的管理來餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人是肥胖 , 同時也是十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這些都不太合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球80%的糧食交易現在只由五家跨國企業所掌控 , 這是很嚴峻的狀況 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們搬到城市裡 , 全世界也接受了西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答一個較簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 是在古老的近東 , 也就是所謂的肥沃冰淇淋 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大約同時發生在同一個地方 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是巧合 , 因為農業和城市是相互連結的 。 它們彼此需要 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先首次發現穀物 , 它能產生足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們就會發現它們很緊密 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農田包圍 , 被像烏爾這樣的神廟大型神廟所統治 , 實際上 , 是精神化的 , 中央食品分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排收穫 , 收集穀物 , 獻給眾神 , 再提供給眾神的穀物 , 讓眾神們不再吃東西 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活 , 主要是穀物和收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元前一世紀 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市要如何餵飽自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸到大海 , 這使得羅馬可以從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在遠古時期唯一能做到這一點的辦法 , 因為要把食物運送到馬路上是非常困難的 , 這條路很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就壞掉了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動了戰爭 , 針對像卡瑟和埃及這類的地方 , 來取得他們的穀物儲備 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張實在是相當長的軍事化的購物中心 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我得提一下羅馬實際上是從倫敦出口牡蠣的一個階段我覺得這很特別
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬以牠的食慾塑造了牠的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦地圖在十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物是從泰勒那裡出來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路上的道路由它們導向便宜的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街道 , 你可以看出三百年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然是從河裡出來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯門特是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真是不平凡 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人帶著手機到處走 , 看起來就像磚塊 , 聞起來像港口的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	另一件關於城市食物的食物:一旦它進入城市的根源被建立起來 , 它們就幾乎不會動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類則截然不同因為動物可以走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	它來到倫敦西北區 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位於那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽是從東安格利亞到東北部的 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女人在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類用腳來保護牠們的腳 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當牠們到達便宜區域的東端時 , 牠們就被賣掉了 , 所以被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下在工業時代之前所建造的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所形塑的 , 通過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前的日子裡你會在星期五去買魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一被買賣食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年的史密斯菲爾德的照片你會發現 , 住在像這樣的城市很難過而且你會不知道你的食物從哪裡來的
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你的午餐時間是星期日 , 可能是三天前在你的窗外 , 心情或呼吸 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 屬於有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物就不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	它們被從視覺和思想中被屠殺 , 在鄉下的某個地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們用鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	一開始 , 它使得城市第一次能夠成長 , 任何大小和形狀都可以 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市被地理限制 ; 以前 , 城市必須通過艱難的身體來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們就從地理上解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦地圖上的倫敦 , 火車出現後的九十年 , 它從一個很容易餵飽的小點 , 由動物用腳餵飽的小點 , 如此一來 , 大量的噴泉 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 不論是動物或人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了汽車之後 , 這整個過程就結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後解放 , 完全是從自然界的任何明顯關係中解放出來的 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市沒有嗅覺 , 沒有混亂 , 當然也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想著要走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	實際上 , 他們把食物送進車裡 , 開車到郊區的箱子裡 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想著到底該怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	而這正是我們與食物及城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了我們和城市之間的關係 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有食物 , 過去是市中心 , 周邊城市的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	過去是一場社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前煮飯時 , 只是加水 , 或加一點蛋 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需讀包裝背後的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	與其珍視它 , 我們就把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統最諷刺的一點就是它們已經做出了承諾 , 讓事情變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過讓城市能夠在任何地方、任何地方建立城市 , 它們其實已經讓我們和最重要的關係遠離了 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且它們也讓我們依賴只有它們能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 這種系統是不穩定的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯就這麼問自己了 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的首映 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列半自主的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一個日子走出來 , 每個人基本上都是農業 , 在自家後園種植蔬菜 , 一起吃公共餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想 , 你可以主張食物是烏托邦的根本原則 , 即使更多人從未用那樣的方式來形容它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 觀點 , 伊伯內斯•霍華茲 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 周圍有可耕地的小都會區 , 被鐵路連接在一起 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物也可能是他提出願景的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但與默斯克韋茲的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的點子問題就在於它們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是一個湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這有點開玩笑 , 因為希臘語有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能是指好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是想像的 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出另一種選擇 , 即希托邦 , 來自古希臘 , 古希臘文 , 意思是 「 食物和地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西索比亞 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物當作一個非常強大的工具 , 一個概念化的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 這只是狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活的中心 , 家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間來讚頌 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物就在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有這樣的人 , 否則你不可能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	有人會想到食物 , 他們會先計畫 , 可以盯著一堆生的蔬菜 , 並認出這些蔬菜 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為若沒有這樣的人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	我故意選這個 , 是因為它是個男人在買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 食物在當地生長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社交生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這些 , 你就無法擁有這種地方 , 當地生長的食物 , 同時也是景觀的一部分 , 而不只是從未見過的零和商品中消失 。
cows with a view .	牛則帶著景象 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸氣堆積的謙遜 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把所有的東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區項目 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	那是一間溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有有關食物和種植食物的一切 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫做凱文的植物 , 或者它是屬於凱文的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這種企劃將我們與大自然重新連結的專案非常重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 它承認希托邦已經存在於各地的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	秘訣是要加入它們 , 用食物當作一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不會把城市視為是大型、大都市化、沒有生產力的團體 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地被連結在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是一個很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再這樣生產糧食 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入地思考永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖可以為我作個總結 , 並且我們需要做些什麼 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最佳影像來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉下的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這一點的訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 這個國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要問大家 , 如果他把這張照片畫出來 , 安布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂會怎麼畫 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	一個良好政府的寓言今天看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的問題 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為非常強大的工具 , 來更好地塑造這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	從慈悲憲章開始的幾週 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯研究了在二十一世紀宗教的角色:它的教條會把我們分開嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們團結起來嗎 ? 她會檢視促進世界的信仰 , 重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	神、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal , 2009年的暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們恢復黃金法則吧 !
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教的歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心在世界上的主要信仰的中心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都進化出他們自己所謂的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時它會出現在正面的版本中 , 「 總是在對待別人 , 就像你想要被對待自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做你不希望他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看自己的內心 , 去了解痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去打擊別人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則如孔子所說的: 「 一整天、每一天 」 , 不只是一個做好事的日子 , 然後返回貪婪和自我主義的生活 , 而是一整天都在做 , 把自己從世界的中心深化 , 再放到另一個 , 然後超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	這就帶你到一個名為 「 神 」 、 「 nirvana 」 、rama、tao的場合 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的超越我們自主的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道這對宗教生活來說是如此重要
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 他們會爭論墮胎的教義 , 或是說出一堆仇恨或歧視同性戀的議會之類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不希望有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士談話時 , 有一種很不一樣的表情 , 會穿越他們的臉 , 因為人們通常希望是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然是違反了運動的目標 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我如此感謝ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書中學習 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和比我想像更廣大的觀眾對話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這很迫切 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不打算在全球實施黃金法則 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 都有可能是誰 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	反而宗教應該要做出重大貢獻 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 宗教不只是相信黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種充滿想像力的行為 , 將自己置於另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 似乎對我而言 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續提出或強調我們的信仰的教條和不寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比 , 上古老的猶太人希爾 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 他會向這整個猶太人教導 , 說: 「 你不該對你做什麼 , 不要對你的鄰居做任何事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉 , 其他的都只是評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	猶太教的早期祖父拉比和教會的早期父親說任何對聖經的詮釋都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要恢復那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛情的精神讓我們不知所措 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切成真 , 藉由ted介紹的現代溝通 , 我們可以做到這一點 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 有一群人要用憲法來治癒最近在新加坡社會出現的分裂 , 一些國會議員想要用政治的方式實現它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展會 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們、年輕人 , 向他們展示慈悲也是一切藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲 , 穆斯林社區舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有宗教的中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們出錯的地方 , 僅僅是相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教的教學必須採取行動 。

but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但如果你只是想一想 , 你就不會了解同情心 。

i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 幫助我們解決一些別人刻板印象的觀點 , 這些觀點讓我們彼此分裂 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也是一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能夠感受到動態 , 一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。

i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要呼籲學者 , 呼籲他們探索同情心的議題 , 用他們自己和其他人的傳統 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是要鼓勵人們對無情言論的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺少信仰 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不友善的言論 , 不友善的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 不友善的言論 。

he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區分愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他將之與友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁時 , 肩並肩 , 目光固定在共同的目標上 。

and i am convinced .	我深信不疑 。

unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 對她來說 , 主線纏繞著某些男孩的偵察隊 , 他們正在參觀萬神殿 , 他們馬上就被拉出來 , 帶到一趟非凡卻又駭人的旅程 , 參觀羅馬的一些穹頂 , 從他們的角度看 , 很自然就會被上下顛倒 。

unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 那是個問題:它們靠得太近了 , 而當你在一個可怕的位置時 , 你必須非常小心提高峰量 。

marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬塞羅是個懶人 , 但他一直到中午都在工作 。

he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳上他的小摩托車 , 穿過城市 , 穿過聖母院 , 穿過巷道 , 穿過街道 , 遊客可能會在街道上遊蕩 , 每次轉彎 , 讓羅馬的安靜的後座生活變得不安 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	那個他正在移動的速度 , 我希望我已經建議了這個小圖像 , 同樣地 , 它可以轉過來從兩邊閱讀 , 因為下方有文字訊息 , 上面有一張是倒過來的圖片 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一位毫無疑問的服務員 , 他正試著用兩盤精心設計的白葡萄酒蛤醬 , 送到餐廳外的餐廳餐廳吃飯 。

removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	移除一些支架 。 羅馬依然保留非凡之處的原因之一是 , 因為支架和維持布料的決心 , 羅馬依然生長適應特定時間的需求 , 羅馬才是這個城市 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	透過廣場德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神殿的前面 , 再次殘破不堪 , 終於開始著手 。

he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他有蠟燭 , 中間有鮮花 , 他試著找出放置板子和玻璃在哪裡 。

he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後慢慢地他走到樓頂 , 公寓 , 檢查每一台電視機 , 希望能找出問題的所在 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	終於 , 他爬上大樓 , 然後爬上小一點的樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一塊桌布圍繞著大樓的電視天線 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在所要做的 , 只剩下一張完美的桌子 , 就是等著她來 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠傳達我想要表達的關於羅馬的意願 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我只會做廣場 , 然後我會進到裡面、下面我會展示這些東西的形狀 , 並展現出它們的形狀等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我只會拿我最喜歡的位元和片段 , 然後把它們放進萬神殿裡 , 留下尺度 , 這樣你就能看到聖雅圖的頂端以及塞西提烏斯金字塔 , 還有布拉曼特的寺廟 , 一邊站在這個神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	現在這只是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮納西認識escher了
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我已經失去了控制 , 失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很薄的藍色的疲勞路線 , 會貫穿整條路線 , 讓路線連接在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不僅僅是收集資料和儲存資料的好方法 , 還包括了一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把另一層剝開 , 我們認為它們是頁面 , 以某種特定的方式呈現 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它想成是層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個地平線地層 , 垂直地層 , 我心想 , 只要從頁面上剝下一層 , 就可以讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 讓我呈現出它的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物牆上的黏土覆蓋了圍巾 ; 經過幾個世紀的變化 , 因為這些建築物的適應力而不是被拆掉 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺紙頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 看看我所說的疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製作小窗戶是不可或缺的 , 因為壞人會來 , 諸如此類 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應性都被埋在了黏土之下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazzo的頁面給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能讓你們看看 , 那些壯觀的建築的角落 , 和那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊和泥土所做的假石塊塊 , 比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從那些窄小的街道帶到其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 利用雙門摺疊的紙張 , 如果你和我一樣小時候讀一本彈起書 , 希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭的頁面包起來 , 就會在那短暫的時間內出現在廣場 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我並沒有做任何比摺紙更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神殿和前方的廣場 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開整本書 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們就在俯視萬神殿的正面 , 往下看 , 大概是從正方形上往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書反過來 , 我們會看到廣場的正面 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何秘訣 , 只有一本不完全開明的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	看來很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會把它內部做出來 , 我甚至可以把摺疊書和唯一部分開放的書做結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神殿 , 以此類推 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我站在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了它的人性 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓大家注意一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 那一定是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我印象深刻 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是隻寄生的鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題是可行的 , 使用它 。 但這將會是一次穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示我喜歡的羅馬的一切 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天起床 , 做些正常的鴿子事 。 回來 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色網路包覆著 , 沒有辦法讓這隻鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	這是隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個適合居住的地方 , 這樣才能讓我通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從較高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它還得回去和家人住在一起 。 這不一定是好事 , 但它確實能讓鴿子再次聚集在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有個人應該要參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方去找危險的地方 , 什麼都不會 , 他們和這個傢伙變成真正的朋友 , 並在午餐時間和他玩耍 , 諸如此類 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	老人和鴿子之間有著真實的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事的結尾真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 阿爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天沒見過他之後的某一天出現 , 他住在這個小車庫裡 , 他們拼他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 能爬上梯子 , 爬到屋頂上 , 所有鴿子 , 一隻紅色的氣球 , 都在等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到:每當他丟了一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子送到城牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋藏在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很棒的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會有很長的路要走
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有傳播到哪裡 , 我只想出了標題 , 希望書名能把我踢向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它的確會把我集中在一個標題頁上 , 我甚至會畫一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些都是書名頁面 , 最終讓我找到了解決方案 , 故事是關於一位年輕女子 , 她把信息傳遞給一位在羅馬城牆外的人 , 給城市裡的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	這隻鴿子正飛越這裡的阿巴尼亞山脈
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松果 , 一路上都是如此 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你就會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得必要且可行 , 試圖傳達那種感覺 , 沒有移動 , 飛越城市 , 感覺會是什麼樣子 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔這些對你來說似乎很熟悉即使你最近沒有去羅馬渡過羅馬大門
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大多數對鴿子最不感興趣的事:它走了一條視野路線 , 我覺得這個裝置需要真的將這本書延伸到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	我們環繞羅馬競技場 , 越過宇宙中的聖母堂 , 以及海克力士神殿 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazzofarnes設計的米開朗基羅的石頭碰撞 , 它是從羅馬競技場被拿來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰柬埔寨的fiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是完全架構的 , 完全否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 有幾個在火星上 , 還有幾個在克雷門 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在廣場上 , 在聖母堂的前方 , 那裡的足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球撞擊 。

i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的部分:聖母堂的速度 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀的翅膀上沒有任何變化 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想知道聖母堂的步調 , 這些書就很有彈性、非常互動性 , 只要把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過這條小巷 , 我們可以看到影響力被記錄在紅線上 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥兒藉由中世紀的塔樓把自己拉到一座位在中世紀的塔樓上 , 一座位於聖塔斯教堂附近的中世紀塔樓 , 俯瞰整個中世紀的廣場 , 我們已經看到並飛過好幾次了 。 這裡有四條河流的伯尼斯特雕像 , 經過美妙的聖雅各聖雅各神廟 , 在26英尺的天孔上停止了足夠長的時間 , 直達我們的天堂 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們會不斷地轉動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用在特定的時刻 , 擔心地心引力 , 這樣這幅圖就能在頁面上隨心所欲地轉動 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們穿越gesu時 , 我們會有點開心 ; 用這種方式模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過了一道美麗的牆壁 , 充滿了我之前提到的混合體 ; 美麗的雕刻會被放在 「 崛起 」 的牆壁上 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們到了帕拉佐島的院子 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	牠從鳥的腿上移除訊息 , 牠是這樣說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們看到他正在畫的是鴿子走過的旅程地圖 , 紅線穿過了所有畫面 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員skylartibbits是自行組裝的概念是 , 與其建造東西 , 我們可以創造出材料 , 讓它們自己建立 , 和一股dnazips本身的方式是一樣的 。 這是一個大的概念 。 tibbits告訴我們三個自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空tibbits:我們能製造出能製造出自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想要向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快地 , 我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復它們 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我會告訴各位 , 我相信是目前的製造業狀態 , 接著將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業階段 , 我們有摩天大樓二年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、嶄新、令人振奮的鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃技術 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空--250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或有三十億鹼基對的dna , 在大約一個小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們能修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式就有令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中使用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是建築物如何運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的部分 , 可以使用該序列來進行摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能激活這些能量 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的矯正措施 , 以確保我們已經成功地建構出我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我的麻省理工學院同事和我正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是巨型機器人和決策機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些專案是大規模的可重組的機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被機械式電器和感應器嵌入其中 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼你想要摺的東西 , 成一連串的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 120 , 120 , 負120 , 類似的東西--所以一連串的角度 , 或轉彎 , 然後你就把這序列列列列列送進去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都帶著它的消息--負120--它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的帶來了光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人小時都為了這八呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人深植到每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 看看被動的本質 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可程序性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試著實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了最基本的計算阻礙 , 數位邏輯 , 直接嵌入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 就是將要運算的大門 , 你有兩個輸入四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 正如你在建構你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個則是從先前被安置的磚塊中 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間的輸出值 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它以前的做法 , 和你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 上或下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入值等於產出0 , 輸出值會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 輸出值會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的信息嵌入其中 , 包括建構的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱之為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的信息都嵌在其中 , 告訴你如何修正它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有爬上去讀的東西 , 並且在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有外部的指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以 , 我將要展示的最後一個專案叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是目前被動自我組裝系統中最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全相同 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
