so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每一個單位是否應該向左或向右轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它就會摺疊成任何你編程的配置 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者 , 在這個例子中 , 兩個彼此旁邊的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以設計任何立體形狀或單面的二維向上 , 完全被動地進入這條鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以這告訴我們什麼關於未來的問題 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想這告訴我們 , 有新的自我組裝、複製、修復的可能性存在於我們的物理結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些區域有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那裡你就有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器、所有磚塊都能計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的平行電腦運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	這對這點來說是很刺激的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛剛展示的這些專案 , 只是朝向這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們能實現這些新技術 , 來創造一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底深處的兩次 。 下一代要探索什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃菲提出了答案:幾乎所有問題 。 然後我們可以開始 , 他說 , 與那些不可置信的小世界一起探索 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾菲:還有什麼要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	為了向一個偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列的探險 , 前往未知的區域 , 就像這裡的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很棒的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說 , 他後來成為印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生進行公開演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 如果有任何東西比在ted演講還要嚇人 , 它會試著去注意一群125分鐘的12歲大的學生的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但其中有一個問題在那之後就一直困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個小女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們當中很多人有一種感覺:地球的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們得要去外太空 , 或深海 , 去尋找重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有什麼值得我們去探索的重要嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想到生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家martinusbeijerinck
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌疾病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中取出受感染的果汁 , 並透過更小的過濾器過濾它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他覺得一定有某種東西比當時所知的最小的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人命了個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒的過程中 , beijerinck真的為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成地球上絕大多數的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式的生命信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關的 , 像是天花的消滅 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類乳突病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們卻不知道組成我們星球上大部分基因信息的生命型態 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 它讓我們能做的不只是滑稽表面 , 還能檢視不同物種的個別基因組 , 還檢視整個代謝體 , 將微生物帶進我們體內、我們身邊 , 以及記錄這些物種的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚之間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在定期這樣做 , 來找出未知爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取下了鼻腔代碼 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸系統的病毒 , 比如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會發現一些常見的疑問當然很多是人類的遺傳信息 , 還有細菌和病毒的信息 , 大部分是從你鼻子裡完全沒有傷害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些非常非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些信息時 , 我們會發現 , 你的鼻子裡大約有20%的基因信息完全不符合任何我們從未見過的東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些真正研究這類資料的小組 , 有一些人開始稱之為信息生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前看過的東西 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多類似的例子
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對來說 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質 , 無法被分類 , 無法和我們以前見過的任何東西做配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得愈來愈精準 , 我們已經確定這資訊是一種生命型態 , 至少當中有些是一種生命型態 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只在嬰兒期 , 卻存在一個非常令人興奮的可能性:埋藏在生命中 , 遺傳信息中 , 是生命中尚未被辨識的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一系列a、t、c、g , 我們可能會發現全新的生命類型 , 像beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的思考方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許這能讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症的原因 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的爆發病源頭 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地告訴大家 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們一起合作 , 我們正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 探索新生命存在的生物暗物質 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝我們可能完全沒察覺到在我們眼前的新階級的生活 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能繪製了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有其它地方可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事為下一代的探險家提供了重要的一課 , 給了來自威斯康辛州貝洛伊特的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們把這一課說出來 , 它就像這樣:不要假設我們現在認為有完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追尋你選擇探索的任何領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊無所不知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇的科學家大衛•迪迪希把理論物理學放在背部 , 討論一個更迫切的問題:人類的生存 。 他說 , 要解決全球暖化的第一步 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	我們在宇宙中的位置大衛•德雷迪希 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出義肢 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 歷史上大部分的記錄都以此聞名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球、太陽系、環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的 , 可以維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像以前被認為的、現在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 而內部則是我們賴以生存的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都知道的事 , 和人類歷史大部份的歷史相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學汙垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事 , 都有點像是在說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你認為這兩者是深切的真理 , 要靠自己生活 , 要告知你人生的決策 , 那麼它們看起來會有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能完全阻止他們兩者的錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們環顧四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是朝著同一方向走幾百英哩 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽系 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為星星是從星系來的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大多數地方 , 宇宙中的一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 巨大的銀河系中有螺旋手臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然離宇宙中典型的地方不遠 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達典型的地點 , 你必須走一千倍到達星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在極大的代價下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現在星系間空間的景觀 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 讓大家看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	不是很完美 , 在星系間的空間中 , 漆黑了 , 漆黑了 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	非常黑暗 , 如果你正盯著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星就像超新星爆炸 , 而你正直盯著它看 , 當光線照射到你的時候 , 你仍然無法看到任何閃爍的光芒 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙有多大、有多黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 非常傑出 , 它會讓你在好幾光年的範圍內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常冷 , 絕對零度以下不到三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	真空的空間 。 真空的密度比目前地球上最好的科技所能製造的高一百萬倍 。 這就是典型的地點與這個地方的差異 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方就是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈光打回來嗎 ? 謝謝
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道一個如此遙遠的環境 , 和我們熟悉的如此不同 , 如此陌生 , 如此陌生的環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那到底是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 再往遠處看 , 比我剛才所說的還要遠我是指從這裡 , 用望遠鏡看 , 你會看到一些看起來像星星的東西
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 方形 」 。 方形原本是指方形的物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著有些東西看起來有點像星星 , 但不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 十億年前 , 十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質倒塌了 , 直到超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了重力崩塌的一些能量 。 有些物質以巨大的噴射流形式呈現 , 照亮了葉片的光芒--我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現今 , 人類大腦的物理性質可能更不像這種噴射流的物理性 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活一瞬間 。 當試著描述其中一次噴射流的狀況時 , 語言會崩解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	可能有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在瞬間 , 以及數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	儘管如此 , 數十億年後 , 這種噴射流在宇宙的另一邊 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 並且解釋 , 最重要的是你在現實中所發生的事情 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個四邊形的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是表面的圖像 , 還包含這張圖 , 還包含解釋性的模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠令人驚訝 , 另一個結構類似的就是時間的增長 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體物體 , 儘管它們可能不像彼此 , 儘管它們有著相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越長 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了越來越精準的萬物結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙的其它地方 , 這個中心本身就是整個物理世界的結構和因果的本質 。 所以 , 至於物理世界的架構是如此的不可忽視的 。 物理定律允許這個現象 , 甚至允許這個發生 , 是最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和環境 , 以我們的形式 , 如何取得這種與宇宙其他地方的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金說的有一點是正確的 , 但它的重點是錯的 。 重點是 , 它沒有運用任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特別的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它有三樣東西可以用在我們這裡豐富的事物上 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有物質 , 就無法製造出一台電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 較不明顯 , 但對於開放式的知識和解釋來說 , 同樣重要 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律大約是300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據 , 在數十億年前 , 已經在地球上每一個平方米落下 , 數十億年之後 , 仍然會持續下去 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 都在這裡 , 就我們星球上的真相 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 創造開放式知識的三個前提條件是最低可能的 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	正如我所說的 , 它是空的、冷的、它是暗的、還是暗的 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另外一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在星際空間中 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體是以人類的標準存在的 , 但那仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 這裡有一群科學家致力於創造開放的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	要把氫氣從星系間的空間聚集在一起 , 再轉化成其他元素等等 , 就不太可能了 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個完全可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 除了我們知道如何做 , 還有什麼可能阻礙我們去做這件事呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動供應能源 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應器和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 人類感官還是黑暗的 。 但你要做的就是拿個望遠鏡 , 甚至今天的設計 , 往外看 , 然後你會看到跟我們一樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理的定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學實地考察 , 因為要花好幾億年才能回到最近的有生命的星球 ,
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , 理查--但我從來不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以用每幾億年完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了所有的準備 , 來創造出開放式的知識 。 在宇宙的任何地方 , 任何一個立方體都可以成為我們本人的中心 , 只要我們知道該怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是唯一適宜居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都是如此 。 地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制性因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源充足 , 而知識 , 則是稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點或許我認為應該讓我們覺得自己很特別 。 但也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這也意味著 , 若沒有具體的知識 , 能夠生存下去 , 我們就不會生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年之外的超新星 , 而我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是要對抗大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在研討會上談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們可以生存 , 而且我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於碰運氣 , 而是我們是否時間創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是前所未有的 。 物種總是絕種 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就到此為止 , 絕大多數的物種和文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是運用區分人類和文明的特徵以及其他所有事物的特徵--也就是我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用在當前的一個爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是要說明我所說的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種物理學家 。 說到全球暖化 , 我只是一個層級的人 。 要做的事情是認真看待普遍的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 目前最好的選擇就是阻止二氧化碳排放如京都議定書 , 限制經濟活動及其成本數百億美元的巨大成本 , 那已經是一場災難了 , 任何合理的措施都可能造成的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者所採取的行動甚至還沒有被提出來解決問題 , 僅僅是把它延後一點點 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 以致於在任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能早在1970年代就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放量即將降低數十億人會死亡的冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一課對我來說似乎很明確 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開的辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們不知道的 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難時 , 以及如何以比災難本身的代價來解決問題 , 那麼其實沒有什麼爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防原則 , 可以避免我們還未預知的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不是僅僅是解決問題的立場 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的解藥 , 但那只是我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你鼻子被打了 , 那麼醫學的科學不會教你如何避免穿刺 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再只在預防上尋求治療和專注 , 那麼它也幾乎不可能做到 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在蓬勃發展 , 計劃在各種成本下 , 強制減少氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要以計劃來降低溫度 , 並計劃在溫度較高的地方住 , 不計代價 , 而是有效率且便宜 。 有些計劃存在 , 像是在太空中放置一群鏡子來將太陽光偏移 , 鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力解決這個問題的中心 , 也不是一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	至於我們還沒有意識到的問題 , 解決問題的能力 , 不是無限期避免的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿二塊石塊平板 , 雕刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 「 問題是可解決的 」 。
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一幅是: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家要如何脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅羅•羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 」 , 城市管理區是由一個由國家聯盟統治的 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅默的想法:特區市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個很棒的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來挑個例子 , 綠色襯衫中的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭納爾遜有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以使用先進的科技 , 像手機 , 但卻無法取得一百年的科技 , 來在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以預防雙贏解決方案 , 只要人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人可以取得 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電力公司遵守一條規則 , 電力公司必須以非常低的補助金來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 電價非常低 , 每賣一單位都會損失金錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 資源和動機都沒有 , 不論是用戶還是用戶 , 都沒有 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他認為有另一套規則是有可能的 , 讓企業賺到小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機簽署更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是尼爾森手機公司購買的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電力定價的規則 , 但卻遇到了一連串的抗議 , 來自企業和消費者 , 他們想要維持現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被一些規則困住 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在路燈下讀書 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著想出如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則我們可以發展來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為我們有普遍的抽象洞見可以實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多的選擇 , 以及給予在許多國家中的領導者更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 介紹這兩者之間的對立是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想要給領導者這種選擇 , 例如給總統提高電價 , 移除經濟中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 就會產生張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多選擇 , 那就會給我們一系列改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離困境 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也可以上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則能讓人們持續在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜晚拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 比起它的鄰居 , 它就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人民留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 要意識到北韓和南韓始於一模一樣的法律和法規 , 也要意識到更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	分開後 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致各式各樣的規則走上不同的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變 , 人類可以改變我們彼此互動的規則 , 讓它變得更好 , 或是更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的線
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 相較於這裡的鄰居多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	相較於波多黎各這兩個國家都很黑暗 , 那裡的居民數量是海地或多明尼加共和國的一半 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則之所以不好 , 是因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只有那些規則是不好的 , 因為政府太強大、太壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們就不能撕掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國顯著地展示了與規則合作的潛在和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到剛剛那張圖表中 , 中國是全球高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先進的技術 , 像是鋼、列印、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期有效的規則中 , 鼓勵傳播這些想法 , 一個獲利的動機 , 鼓勵傳播這些想法 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國不再是世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 作為世界上其他國家創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展新的規則 , 中國已經被阻止進步 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入停滯不前 , 放大世界其他地方的收入 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪收入 , 在中國平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到大約3%的氣候變遷 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	經濟成長在中國起飛 , 中國也開始快速地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到夜晚的地圖 , 就會得到線索 , 引導中國的規則發生劇烈的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地方 , 各位可以看到 , 線的邊緣是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是個很小的中國 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都遵循著很不一樣的規則運作 , 和當時其他大陸規則相比 , 這些規則都複製了當時的市場經濟 , 並由英國政府管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸 , 到開始在工作 , 比如縫紉襯衫、做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了進一步提高收入 , 增加技能 , 導致了非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個領導者 , 像是鄧小平可以複製的模型 , 當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們採取的做法是創造出一些特殊的區域 , 從某種意義上來說 , 英國採取的做法是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想參與其中的人有機會參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近設立了四個特別的經濟區域 , 在那裡 , 中國可以來工作 , 城市可以很快地生長在那裡 ; 外國企業也能來這裡做些事 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有台台灣公司製造了你們多數人擁有的iphone , 他們從中國人搬到深圳的勞工 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	經過四個特別區之後 , 共有14個沿海地區都開放了 , 最終證明了這些地方人民可以選擇的成功 , 因為他們提供的利益而聚集在一起 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證明了成功導致了整個經濟體轉向市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在 , 中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一 , 保留人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在適當的尺度上營運 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但村落太小了 , 無法得到你所能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就無法給予一些人機會 , 看看結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市讓你有機會創造出新的地方 , 人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人以良好的規則一起工作時 , 它們就足以獲得所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 我們的提議是 , 我們構想一個叫做 「 特區城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 來建造電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會先僱用那些先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家人 , 那些將來會永遠住在那裡的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 找到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張憲章 , 人們就會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地去做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些是在特許機構捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市 , 那就已經成為這個模型了 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以依靠新的規劃生活 , 但沒有人會被迫活在下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是為領導者做選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者所需要的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作有潛力:國家之間的合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先是建構一個小小的市場模式 , 然後再擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 不經意地 , 英國通過香港的行動 , 減少世界貧窮 , 遠超過我們上個世紀所參與的所有援助計畫 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這樣的夥伴再度複製這個 , 我們就能讓全世界都受惠 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的代表權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的代表權 , 來掌控某些類型的行政權 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始在想: 「 這帶來殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是要意識到 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 那種情緒會產生 , 可能會阻礙我們去追尋、關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 它仍然是不好的 , 它涉及到強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式完全關乎選擇 , 不管是領導人還是那些會在這些新地方生活的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談它如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	拿一位特定的領導人拉爾•卡斯楚為例 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定想到他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做的 , 但他沒有古巴島上的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方一點點亮 , 有著很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一塊區域 , 條約為美國政府負責一塊地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , yankees有很嚴重的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你們不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	在那裡建造一個新的城市 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會支持 。 但這將會是通往現代經濟和國家的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這種模式還能在哪裡試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全了解了一種特區的想法 , 認為人們可以選擇成為一種規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不受強制 , 同時也不受強制的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾 , 那些會來建造港口的投資者 , 在新城市建立道路 , 他們可以做出更有信心的承諾 , 如果他們能和另一個國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排中 , 有點像是信託管理帳戶 , 把土地放在信託管理帳戶中 , 而合夥的國家要負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有許多可以建設新城市的土地 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地上有大量的延伸 , 讓數億人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們概括一下 , 不只1或2個特區 , 還會有數十億的城市 , 或許下一個世紀會有數十億的人口遷移到城市裡 , 會有足夠的土地供給他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們晚上看著燈光 , 有一件事是誤導人的 , 就是 , 視覺上 , 世界上大部分的人都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你為什麼這是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方形 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表的是三十億人居住的城市已經開始佔用的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到長方形底部你會發現現有30億的城市只佔了地球上可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想要為數十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從百分之三的耕地 , 降到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大大減少了人類在地球上的足跡 , 做法是建造更多可以移居的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市有良好的規則 , 就能讓人們安全地從犯罪、疾病、公共衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們能取得基本的設施 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能開始建造第一座特區城市 , 要擴展這個規模 , 才能建造更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	擁有一本手冊是有用的 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是把一些細節寫進這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們讓城市運行 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者去野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設加拿大不只是跟卡斯楚有關的 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也有參與者 , 西班牙也希望古巴想成為四種合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這樣做前所未有的 , 但也很容易解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何提供資金 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是靠著一開始他們所擁有的土地價值大增的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地價值來支付像是警察、法庭、學校體制和醫療體系的收益 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 鼓勵那些幫助建立這塊區域的人 , 並建立起基本規則 , 往正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多其它類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓第一份工作的人負擔得起低成本的建築物 , 像是iphone , 但讓這些建築物的能源效率提高 , 確保它們是安全的 , 這樣他們不會掉入地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節已經被解決 , 但我們這些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經可以分辨出沒有路障 , 沒有阻礙 , 除了失敗的想像力之外 , 能讓我們無法實現真正的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼幸福 , 是因為地球上有很多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當別人發現這些想法時 , 他們就和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物體 , 分享意味著我們每個人的獲利比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:支配我們如何彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 讓我們來設立一個稅收系統 , 來支援一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 我們有土地的所有權 , 可以登記在政府辦公室裡 , 讓大家可以保證它是附屬的 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷創新我們的制度 , 尤其是創新的制度 , 來制定改變規則的制度 , 這樣我們就不會卡住不良的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續向前邁進 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 讓像納爾遜和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	先驅克萊格•凡特從他的史詩級的圓環探險中休息一下 , 來談談他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 目前為止 , 是為了要繪製海洋生物多樣性的地圖 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科技、科技、科技等 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和大海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時間 , 我被幾個人問我關於老化議題的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這是我對此的唯一評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者遠勝於悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在這18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們將如何從解讀遺傳密碼轉變為開始自己寫程式的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前的這個月 , 我們發表了第一系列完全沒有生命的有機體 , 也就是嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年的時間 , 降到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成相同的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾株植物 , 數種昆蟲和數種哺乳動物 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	大約十年前 , 基因組學在這個思考的階段 , 到今年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的測序 , 數百組的排序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從godon和bettymoore基金會取得資金 , 到今年進行130組基因組的測序 , 作為環保生物的副計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 正如我們所見 , 我們幾乎沒有抓住地球上可得的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人不知道 , 因為它們是肉眼看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔了生物量的一半 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許在牛津的人們不太常這樣做 , 但如果你到海裡吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升海水含有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	大約兩年前 , 不到五千種微生物種類被分類 , 所以我們決定要為此做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們展開了二次足球探險 , 進行大型海洋探險 , 嘗試每200英哩採集樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始我們的測試計畫 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 向下美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫跨太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫渡印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是很困難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 部分原因是要幫助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	這些實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是用海水來過濾 , 我們在不同的過濾器中蒐集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 我們可以在24小時內完成一億個字母的基因序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	有了這些 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 人們認為我們的眼睛裡有視覺色素 , 環境中只有一兩種有機體 , 有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎世界上溫暖區域的所有生物 , 都有相同的光感接收器 , 太陽光是它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	現在我們用sloan基金會的資助將這個計畫擴展到空氣中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們每天吸入多少病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機上 , 或在閉合室內 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們通過一些簡單的設備過濾 ; 我們從僅僅一天之內就收集到十億微生物的排名在紐約市的一棟大樓上 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們目前正在進行所有這些測序的測序 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在資料收集方面 , 我們透過加拉巴哥群島 , 發現幾乎每200英哩 , 海洋中的樣本就有極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上是合理的 , 在不同的溫度層面上 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度紅色是溫暖的藍色 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫度和冷水樣本間的巨大差異 , 就富足物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們相當驚訝的事情是這些感應器偵測到不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測它 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些變化非常大 , 從地區到區域都不同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但在最極端的紅外線和紫外線有更多的變化 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因庫是什麼 , 我們收集了所有的數據 , 包括遠離考察 , 代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總計大約有2900萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因家族放到基因家族中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家族的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家族 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但每一種我們採取的新樣本 , 都會對這些新族群產生一條線性時期 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於基礎基因、成分和生命的最早期發現階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的進化樹 , 我們和動物在右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約2900萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物放在一起 , 我們可能就共有不到三萬隻 , 也許還有十多種不同的基因家族 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認爲這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為以基因為中心的觀點或許可以追溯到理查德•道金斯的想法 , 而非以基因為中心的觀點來看 , 這些基因組成的不同結構 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力 , 能夠合成dna的能力 , 和過去十年或二十年間的dna測序速度相同 , 變得越來越快、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對人造基因組學的第一個想法是在1995年我們對第二組基因組進行基因組定序的時候 , 那個想法是從我的血漿生殖器得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們很簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800種 , 再另外500種 , 是否有更小的基因組可以組成最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子就是隨機插入基因編碼的一小片dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因中間 , 就會阻斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 標記了所有可以接受轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但環境是非常重要的 , 而你只能依據環境中的特定基因來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用比較直接的智能方法來處理13種相關的生物基因組 , 我們試著比較它們 , 來看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們找到的只有173個基因 , 適用於所有13個生物 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略其中一種細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展得更廣 , 當我們觀察核心基因大約310組左右時 , 它會擴展得更廣 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以 , 我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 依據你的觀點來看 , 到300到400個基因 , 來自500的最小基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用這些基因建構人造染色體 , 我們必須以一種模擬的方式來進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片區域中 , 合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆斯•史密斯和我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能用兩週的時間來合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 在其序列和生物學上 , 精確度高達100% 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始製造製造出這種病毒粒子 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個人造病毒 , 小兒麻痺病毒一年前就被製造出來了 , 但它只是一個活躍的牙齒 , 它花了三年才被製造出來 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在用來建構自己的硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上就開始關心生物戰事 , 最近我在參議院委員會前作證 , 美國政府設立了一個特殊委員會來審查這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 很重要的是要記住現實 , 而不是人們的想像 , 會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會馬上對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚訝 , 但這種生物的dna並不是有傳染性的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花基因組 , dna本身不會引起感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的問題是 , 安全部門有設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 投入了大量的努力 , 試圖創造生物戰的代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被終止了 , 未來的設計師病毒應該不會有太多的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能發生 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而可能有真核細胞 , 那些我們擁有的細胞 , 在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在做數十種不同的結構 , 因為我們可以改變這些基因到這個人造染色體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把其他的都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們先從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統將這些碎片分解成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	它是從一種生物體中衍生出來的 , 無線電信號可以讓三百萬拉德的輻射停留下來 , 不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	輻射在12到24小時之內 , 它會重新組合它的基因組 , 在它的染色體被炸開之後 , 它就會被炸開 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能因為我們在外太空旅行 , 已經存在了 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是在大約50萬拉德輻射過後的一個玻璃啤酒器 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 而微生物坐在最底層 , 愈來愈開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際情況的照片上面的是一百七十萬拉德斯輻射後的基因組
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全分開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動組裝完成 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人震驚的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 甚至數萬種不同的物種能做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為人造細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們進行的第三項測序的甲烷分子詹納西它生活在沸騰的水溫當中它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它所有的二氧化碳都從環境中吸收回來
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的生物體 , 可以從二氧化碳中存活 , 並從中獲取回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用從石油中取得的碳來進行合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 將它從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物體 , 存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作降低能量來分解水來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	還有許多途徑可以被改造成甲烷代謝 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦特有一項主要的計畫 , 用在挪威的石油 , 來捕捉和轉換那甲烷 , 將其轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因體 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列會修復 , 以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可能可以製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你可以通過篩選來進行篩檢 , 不論是檢查氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 就會受到影響 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用以直接從陽光生產氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 分解複雜糖分解的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中發酵 , 產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在大型實驗室中使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學物質比我們最好的化學家所產生的更複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能量的來源、環境的調節 , 以及可能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年推出了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 審查是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的經文作為法律書籍 , 他們無法找到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以這肯定沒問題 。 最終的擔憂是生物戰場的重要因素 , 但前提是我們要開始進行這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	史隆基金會剛資助了一個多機構的研究 , 來找出社會的風險和利益 , 以及我自己的科學團隊應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正試著建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了威脅生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計出乾淨能源 , 也許能革新發展中國家的做法 , 並提供各種簡單的程序 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛巴多說幸福和成功是源自於一種我們都忽略的特質:我們向過去、現在和未來方向的方向 。 他建議我們用時間校正我們的前一步 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、企業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普津巴多開立一個健康的計畫 , 準時的進行 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密 , 短時間內的想法 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始計時器 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請安靜下來 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 , 結束序列 。 選一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:讓我們調整一下亞當的誘惑原則 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當拜託 , 不要那麼害怕 。 咬一口 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄埃佛 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 , 到底怎麼回事 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 重點是要培養、抗拒 , 是的 , 遲到 , 衝動、現在 , 以及未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 直到結婚 , 感謝喬治布什大多 , 百分之六十 , 讓她們在一年之內停止了性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有採取控制權 。
so much for promises .	多餘的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在來試試四歲小孩 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會付出代價 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	所發生的是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米切爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 在14年後 , 試圖發現這些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	兩種孩子之間有很大的差異 , 他們抗拒的孩子和被大量地產的孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒分數高出250分的孩子坐在座位上 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很龐大 。 這就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是有自信和堅定的 。 今天我要說的關鍵是 , 他們是以未來為中心的 , 而不是以現在為中心 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時光觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你經歷的流向分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動且無意識地去做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	不同文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水準之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你會學會過度使用它們 , 其他的則會弱化 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做出的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做出一個決定 , 決定你要採取什麼行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 這只關乎當下的狀況 , 其他人的行為 , 以及你的感受 。
