and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過什麼樣的情況 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們關注的是 「 過去式 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於期待的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱它們為 「 未來導向 」 。 它們的重點是未來式 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀的悖論 , 是會影響你做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏頗的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個方法可以用兩種方式呈現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被懷疑 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面的 , 或是過去的負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 " 享樂主義者 " , 也就是你專注於享受人生的樂趣 , 或者 " 現實主義者 " , 這並不重要 , 你的人生被控制住了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來導向的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維靈活性 , 來轉換時間觀點 , 根據情況的需求 , 這是你必須學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度積極正面、適當的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	並且適應當下的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠不論是負面的還是當前的 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最理想的暫時性混合就是你從過去積極的經驗中得到的 , 會給你根源 。 你將你的家人、身份和你的自我聯繫起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的是翅膀 , 飛到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的能量 , 探索自己的地方、人、感官的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過渡時間的觀點 , 都有比正面更負面的觀點 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲快樂的時光 , 犧牲自己的寬容 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 , 這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、成就和控制而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信會和一些ted觀眾產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這讓我產生共鳴 。 我小時候在南布朗士貧民窟長大 , 一個西里島家庭 , 大家都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來導向的人 , 走到頂端 , 做這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等到你會得到兩顆 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了當下主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的正面 , 所以 , 在76歲的時候 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我也比以往更開心 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們把這套應用在許多世界問題上:輟學率 , 戒掉成癮率 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 來促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體康復率 , 降低自殺率 , 改變自殺式恐怖份子的狀況 , 修正家庭衝突期限 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想以此作結:生命中的許多謎題可以藉由理解你的時間觀和他人的時間觀來解開 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果是非常深遠的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條在一百年後會有多少影響 ? 1000年 ? 柯林頓的 「 長期新聞 」 專案計畫收集到現今不但很重要的數十年 , 還會共鳴數十年 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了近期的頭條新聞標題 , 有可能塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學等 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在則是真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社一年就刊出了三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 到底有多少故事是很重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是長期的現在基金會 , 由tedsters成立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特蘭 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞報導可能在50、100或10 , 000年之後仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多東西會從旁邊掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年p.的頂尖故事來說 , 這在十年內很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會有影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的頭條是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 不論遲早 , 這次的經濟衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液流 , 去修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 那天早就在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些近期的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真實的蜜蜂毒液將基因送到腦部 , 一個可以在人體上爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今 , 餵養六十億人是有問題的 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國若沒有修改過的作物 , 就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茨有10億人在研究農業 。
what about global politics ?	那麼 , 全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	如果中國設立議程 , 世界就會變得很不一樣 , 可能的話 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越了美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越了德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始對孩子進行dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法 , 來回推動我們所知道的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有項來自阿根廷的蟻群遍佈各大洲 , 但南極 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家很快地發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命可能也不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎 , 有沒有我們 , 生命會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但是我去年的長篇新聞是這個:在月球上發現了水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓殖民地更容易被殖民 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能會 , 或許在這間房間裡有人會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco顯示了卡西尼航行到土星的圖片 , 著重在它最大的衛星泰坦 , 以及冰凍的土衛二 , 這類圖像似乎能拍攝到冰噴射 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco讓我們飛到土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是你和我多年來的旅程 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不但真的登上了月球 , 我們還把機械飛行器送到所有八個行星上 , 我們在小行星上著陸 , 登陸了彗星 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空飛船 , 前往冥王星的途中 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解地球 , 我們和地球的生命 , 來實現 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 。 土星 。 我們去過土星 。 1980年代早期我們去過土星 , 但我們對土星的研究越來越深入 , 自從卡西尼號太空船開始 , 橫跨星際空間七年之久 , 在2004年的夏天 , 滑進土星的軌道 , 成為人類歷史上最遙遠的機械人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 以及明顯的相對光明 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單單研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星球的圓形和氣體的資訊 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是andromedanebula美麗的照片這是我們銀河系中最接近的最大螺旋星系
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	再來 , 這是由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的一個美麗的旋轉星系 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 其實是一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 象徵了人類更大的旅程 , 來了解我們身邊一切事物的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入那張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們在卡西尼身上學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示過去兩年半我們拍過的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我會把焦點放在這次重大探險旅程中最令人興奮的兩段故事 , 過去兩年來 , 我們一直在土星進行 , 已經持續了兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著大而多樣化的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里寬 , 一直到美國這麼大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍過土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和一些衛星同行 。 這是土星和土星 。 這是土星和土星 。 這裡是土星 , 展示了邊緣的光環 , 讓你知道它們有多薄 , 垂直的恩克拉多斯 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	47顆土星的衛星中有兩顆是立體行星 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二土衛二 。 土衛二是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號抵達那裡 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	牠的身體 , 長久以來一直很好奇那些看過地球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像是地球上的環境 , 或者說至少過去 , 在太陽系中的任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中含有大量氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮 , 只不過它的大氣中含有簡單有機物質 , 比如甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	泰坦大氣中的這些分子會被分解 , 它們的產品會結合在一起 , 形成霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物無所不在 , 它是全球性的 , 密封土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼我們不能用肉眼看到表面 , 用肉眼可見的光譜區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒在我們抵達卡西尼號之前就被保證了 , 經過數十億年 , 經過數十億年 , 緩慢地移向地表 , 把表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機堆中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	像泰坦一樣 , 焦油 , 油 , 或我們不知道的東西 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六表面溫度的液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷會讓土衛六上的水流到地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是凝聚的 , 所以認識到這種情況 , 帶來了奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 有數百公里的霧霾 , 可以防止任何陽光進入地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管溫度很低 , 土衛六上還是會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 降雨對地球造成的影響:它能雕刻地殼 ; 它會形成河流和瀑布 ; 它能形成峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和坑洞中澆水 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥土從高山的山峰和山坡上沖到低地 。 所以停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它很暗 。 土衛六上的中午跟地球上擦拭的深海一樣暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 很噁心 , 很可能會下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖的密西根湖邊 , 油漆很薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達之前所看到的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現了什麼 , 雖然它的細節並不相同 , 但它的所有吸引力都和故事一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是叢林凡爾的探險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 由太陽照射 , 環則是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另一顆衛星我甚至不知道是哪一顆衛星 。 它是非常廣大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 能透過大氣層看到地面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 大約在它為我們抵達的最遙遠的地方 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太神秘了:我們無法搞清楚我們在土衛六上看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你更靠近這個區域 , 你就會開始看到一些東西 , 如同我們不知道的 , 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 這其實是一座火山 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少的隕石坑 , 意思是說 , 它的地表很年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來是構造的 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個星球上有線性的東西時 , 它就意味著有著像斷了一樣的骨折 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以在地質上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件事情發生了 , 很多人都認為是卡西尼號對土衛六的高峰調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯探測器的部署 , 歐洲的惠更斯探測器在整個太陽系內運行了七年之久 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時才下降 , 它降到地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是一個人類製造的裝置 , 它第一次登陸在外太陽系 , 這是人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這非常重要 , 在我心中 , 這是一個活動 , 應該要在美國和歐洲各地的城市中 , 用貼紙遊行來慶祝 。 很遺憾的是 , 事情並沒有發生 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這對另一個原因來說意義重大 。 這是一項國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國 , 和慶祝的演講被用英文口音、美國口音、德國語、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音表達 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個動人的示範 , 說明了 「 聯合國 」 應該有的意義:一個真正的聯合國團結起來 , 集合了一大筆的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探測一個星球是很大量的 , 想要了解一個星球系統 , 這個星球系統在整個人類歷史上一直是不可靠的 , 而現在人類已經觸摸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我談到雞皮疙瘩了 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 我永遠不會忘記這件事 , 你們也不應該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器測量了大氣層下降的過程 , 也測量了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器看到土衛六表面的第一張照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是個震撼人心 , 因為那是我們想要其他照片的 , 從軌道拍攝到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一個明確的模式 , 一個地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種樹狀的排水模式 , 只因為液體的流動而形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以遵循這些管道 , 你可以看到它們是如何結合在一起的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們聚集在這裡 , 流入這片區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里高的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 同樣地 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好吧 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要乘飛機穿越美國 , 你就要飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是土衛六航空公司的窗口 , 當你飛越土衛六時 ,
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於在地表上安息 , 我將展示給各位看 , 各位先生女士 , 這是第一個從外太陽系月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有沉沒在視野中 。 所以它不是我們著陸的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器下降的狀況等同於一片泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一塊未整合的地 , 被液態甲烷所包圍 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是因為這種材料已經透過我們看到的這些管道沖刷了土衛六上的高地 , 花了數十億年才填滿了低窪地帶 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像中仍沒有標誌 , 或甚至惠更斯影像中的任何大型的流體都沒有標誌 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	它們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 它更讓人費解了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六區域的影片 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 被幾個公里的沙丘分開 , 延續好幾英里的距離 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	那裡有數百個沙丘 , 高達一千到一千個沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 這個地方很乾燥 , 否則你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	同樣的 , 這也讓人感到困惑 , 沒有任何液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了北極的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	這是土衛六南極的一個湖泊地
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大小約跟安大略湖一樣大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 一個禮拜半前 , 我們飛越了北極土衛六 , 發現了同樣的 , 我們發現了一種特徵 , 大小和加勒比海一樣 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 不知為何 , 不知為何 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 土衛六的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們應該會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個不可思議、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 但卻很像地球 , 擁有類似地球的地質構造和極其豐富的地質多樣性 。 這是一個非常迷人的世界 , 一個在太陽系中唯一與複雜及豐富宇宙相對的宇宙 , 就是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大約是鐵衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它旁邊的英國 , 給你看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 非常明亮 , 土衛二的表面有很明顯的破裂 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它在地質上是非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多是在南極發現的 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 在這裡 , 我們發現了骨折系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些裂縫被有機物質覆蓋著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極區域的溫度上升了 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 發現地球南極比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍了額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些裂縫中 , 會產生出微小、冰粒 , 延伸到太空中數百英哩的噴射 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將圖像顏色區分出來 , 呈現出微弱的光線 , 我們可以看到這些噴射噴射噴射的光譜 , 事實上 , 在其它影像中 , 噴射到距離土衛二上數千英里的空間 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊探討了像這樣的影像 , 像這張 , 想過卡西尼公司的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射流可能會從土衛二表面下的液態水噴發出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質 , 以及過多的熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的神聖地表 , 換句話說 , 對於有機體而言 , 可能是很合適的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 其他地方發現生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有龐大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明創世紀的發生不只一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立發生了兩次 , 那就意味著 , 根據推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了無數次的次數 , 以及它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一一個充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它依然是我們至今唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們其中任何人在1960年代有警覺和連貫 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你沒有 , 好 , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空中拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對於地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	卡西尼號首先拍下了一個人眼前從未見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張極其美麗的照片中 , 你看到太陽的主要光環 , 會看到反射太陽的影像 , 你會看到這個光環 , 事實上 , 是由土衛二的廢氣排放出來的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的影像中發現我們自己的星球 , 塞滿了土星光環的手臂 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一種深深的感動關於從遠處看自己 , 並捕捉到我們在其他星球的天空中的小藍色的行星 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 我們從那得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這次探索旅程中得到的最好的獎賞 , 大約是半個世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 全世界僅有15%的人被繪製出地圖 。 災難後遞送的援助慢下來 , 隱藏未知的道路經濟潛力 。 在這簡短的演說中 , 谷歌已故的卡達達示威者地圖 , 全球各地的人正在繪製他們的地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 科技 , 科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 颶風納基人毀滅了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要運送人力和補給品到這個地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 也沒有辦法幫助惡性循環受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 我們很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地圖是對應到可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國跑到一個世界大部分的人口臉孔問題上:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救命來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40名志工用新軟體繪製出12萬公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 運輸系統和救濟點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 讓每個人能夠繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流、學校、當地企業、錄影商店到轉角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人赫爾•德•索托意識到 , 對大部分發展中國家來說 , 經濟的關鍵是要利用大量未經記載的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光是在印度就有一兆美金的房地產是不合資的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家的數千名使用者就已經繪製出了數百萬筆資訊 , 並繪製出了從未想過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這點之所以能實現 , 是因為各地充滿熱情的使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們來看看一些由使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們在繪製地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛繪製了塞內加爾的道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近的是chlua , 班加羅爾的g路線 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是對70%未被開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦的巴勒斯坦村莊進行非暴力抗議 , 阻止他們在他們的橄欖爐上建設一道障礙 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 沒有這麼想 。 巴西的電影製作人朱利亞•巴查查查問為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突中的暴力 , 而不是非暴力領袖 , 他們有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、影片、和平、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞•巴夏:注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人試圖用和平手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國各地旅行時 , 總是有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我通常才剛從中東回來 , 我拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試圖打造大規模的非暴力運動 , 終止佔領 , 在該區域建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂存在於各地發生的事和感知之間 , 正是造成我們尚未擁有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來這裡是要談關注的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩 , 以及其他地方的發展 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力的成長 , 並不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力的方式 , 而是我們開始注意那些已經是誰 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我帶你到一個叫做布德鲁斯村的村莊來闡明這個觀點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要建造出一個隔離障礙 , 部分的障礙會建在村落的上方 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被環繞 , 這樣他們就會失去自由地進入西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地受到鼓舞的領導 , 他們發起了和平抗爭活動 , 阻止了這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以明白地上到底是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆會分離巴勒斯坦和以色列 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男人:這道柵欄實際上已經為恐怖創造出一個解決方案
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:沒有什麼比非暴力反對者更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試著推動士兵 , 但他們沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空我們傳統思維的想法 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號聲:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和大眾前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍籬的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像失敗一樣 , 到處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但 , 我身邊也有其他人甚至沒有勇氣 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止這場戰爭 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	茱莉亞•巴查:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很訝異國際媒體沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更讓人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民在十個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服了以色列政府 , 將他們土地的路線移走到綠線上 , 也就是國際公認的以色列和巴勒斯坦領土間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗藥性從此流傳到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事很沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力事件的發展 , 或甚至在巴勒斯坦的可能性有著深遠的影響 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 ; 它們都是某種形式的戲院 , 想要讓觀眾致力於他們的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力行動者是唯一不斷得到頭版的人 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦問題 , 對非暴力領袖來說 , 就很難向他們的社區證明公民不服從是可行的選擇 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在座的父母一點都不驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓你的孩子越來越吵鬧的方式是給予他第一次的注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	反覆思考會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為這個孩子學到 , 他能從中得到父母的關注 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予或不給予孩子注意力 , 來鼓勵或不給予行為獎勵 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東的衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 是要把非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 , 做法是讓現今的非暴力領導人更加關注 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片到西岸的村落、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我見到就算是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉jeh的村莊裡 , 這個村莊離耶路撒冷很近 , 村落正面臨著和布德鲁斯村很類似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經在使用非暴力手段兩年了 , 但自從沒有人注意到他們之後 , 他們就漸漸消失了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一份篩檢 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了目前為止最完善且有紀律的示威 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在電影中 , 覺得真的有人在追蹤他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做slidariot , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導者一直在使用布德鲁斯村作為主要的工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人以前從來沒有積極參與過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉jeh和索里德拉蕊運動的例子顯示即使只有小成本的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 如果大型媒體開始報導每週發生的非暴力行為 , 像比利、尼林、瓦拉吉 , 在耶路撒冷的社區中發生的那種力量 , 會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見過 , 如果我們能做到 , 它們就會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以巴衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力就是那種能夠終止現況的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的 , 在布德鲁斯村 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們把注意力交給他們 , 讓他們可以證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•桑克有個簡單但強大的模式 , 能鼓舞人心的領導力從金色圈子開始 , 問 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	野牛、商業、企業家、領導、銷售、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙:偉大的領導者如何鼓舞行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你該怎麼解釋當事情不如我們預期的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠完成似乎違反所有假設的事物時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比其他競爭者更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	但 , 他們只是一間電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	它們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的才華、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼它們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到公民權待遇的人 , 他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控、動力強的飛行器 , 尤其是其他團隊更有資格、更有資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有成功 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、具啟發性的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為、行動、和溝通的方式都是一樣的 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠鼓舞其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這些詞彙 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百知道他們在做什麼 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你怎麼稱呼它為你不同的價值觀提案 , 或你的私人訴訟程序或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 不是指 「 賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的理由是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外部 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事轉變為最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但 , 鼓舞人心的領導者以及鼓舞人心的組織 , 不論它們的規模如何 , 不論它們的產業都會從內而外思考、行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我會用蘋果 , 因為它們很容易懂 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 來自行銷的訊息可能聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們的設計很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」 「 我 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數人行銷的方式 , 多數人行銷的方式 , 多數人行銷的方式 , 多數人和人際溝通的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何變得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們一起做生意的客戶做表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的汽油哩程 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果電腦溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮、很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同 ? 你已經準備好向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	事實證明人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼這個房間裡的每一個人都可以完全舒服地買一台蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一間電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能將它們從結構上分辨出來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面監視器好幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦想出了mp3播放器和pda , 他們做出了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出很完善的設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談這件事 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我跟你們說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都是基於生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的橫向圖 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦其實分成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人 , 我們的新皮層 , 會對應到 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 而我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、益處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內而外的溝通 , 我們直接對著控制行為的腦說話 , 然後我們允許人們去合理化它 , 用我們說且做的事情 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是直覺決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給人事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是什麼 , 但感覺不太對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 它不會說 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部區域不會控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的一點是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你是以心來領導 , 或者你是以你的靈魂來領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想對你說 , 那些不是身體的其他部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這些都發生在你腦袋的邊緣 , 控制決策而非語言的腦部 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你所做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做你所做的事 , 那你就永遠不會讓人們為你投票 , 或從你身上買東西 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠地去做你想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要的人 ; 目標是要賣給相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人 , 而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用員工 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人 , 他們會用血汗、汗水和淚水來為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除了萊特兄弟之外 , 還有更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力飛行的人就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley曾經有過 , 我們認為是成功的關鍵 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三件事:弱勢者、錯誤的人、不好的市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總共有三件事是一樣的 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金的資金來研發這種飛行器 。
money was no problem .	金錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他有哈佛大學的座位 , 在史密森學院工作 , 他認識當時的所有人 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的人才資金 , 市場狀況很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都支持蘭利 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	距離俄亥俄州的幾百英哩遠 , 歐維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功的訣竅 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用他們腳踏車店的旅程來支付他們的夢想 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊沒有一個人接受過大學教育 , 連歐維爾或威爾堡都沒有 ; 紐約時報也跟著他們到處去 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾巴被一個目的、一個目的、一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能找出這台飛行器 , 就能改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不一樣 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟夢想中的人用血汗、汗水和淚水和他們合作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則只是為薪資工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是 , 每次萊特兄弟出去 , 他們就得採取五組零件 , 因為這就是他們出生前墜機的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	直到1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟開始飛行 , 甚至沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們幾天後才發現這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明蘭利的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 各位 , 那是個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你們的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個人 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你的信仰 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的信仰的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某樣東西叫做創意的散播法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你一定會知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數晚期的大多數和已故的笑話
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	只有這些人會買到電話的唯一理由 , 就是你不能再買老式手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都曾坐在不同時間的不同地方在這個尺度上 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不能擁有它 , 直到你在15%到18%之間的市場滲透點 , 然後系統就會跌倒 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你在新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大概是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓客戶超過10% 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 懂了 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像是那種直覺 , 「 噢 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:在你和他們做生意之前 , 你要如何找到答案 ? 還是你沒有得到它的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	正如jefreymoore所說的 , 就是這個小缺口所謂的 「 跨越鴻溝 」 , 因為 , 大部分早期的人都不會嘗試直到別人嘗試它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們對於做出這些直覺決策感到很自在 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加舒服地做出這些直覺性的決定 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不僅是產品的可得性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排了六個小時 , 第一次出櫃時 , 買了一支iphone , 下週你只要走進商店就買下一支手機 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 第一次上映 , 儘管這項技術是不可或缺的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做是因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼 , 只證明你的想法 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做的事來證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的原因是在前六個小時排隊排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們希望每個人都能看見:他們是第一人 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 和一個有名的創新散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 知名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們前面所說的 , 第二個問題 , 成功的秘訣就是金錢 , 合適的人和合適的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo八九年前到現在的這一天 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手放下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西藏在垃圾時期華納dvr身上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻失敗了 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們上了ipo , 他們的股票價格大約30到40美金然後就下跌 , 從來沒有在10美元以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它是6以上交易的 , 除了幾個小突點之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們有什麼 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品能暫停現場電視、跳過廣告、轉播現場電視節目 , 還能記住你的收視習慣 , 而且你根本不會去問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活的各個層面的人 , 孩子 , 我們有這樣的產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過商業廣告 , 回憶你的收視習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子關於創新的散播法則
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年的夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何邀請函 , 也沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一位偉大的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個在公民權前受苦的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有份禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們什麼需要改變美國 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的人們接受了他的理念 , 他們讓理念成為他們自己的人 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創建了結構 , 讓更多人聽出來 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在適當的日子出現 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國能讓他們乘坐八個小時的巴士上行八個小時 , 在八月中期站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人 , 是25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世界上有兩種法律:那些由更高權威制定的法律 , 那些由人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有人類的法律都和更高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們會活在一個正義的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正巧如此 , 民權運動才是最佳的幫助他讓他的理由活了下來 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽聽政治人物 , 用全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導的人鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 有能力啟發他們周遭的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記住你車子的位置 ? 你怎麼知道你是往正確的方向走的 ? 神經學家尼爾•漢堡研究了我們身邊空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大型停車場停車時 , 我們怎麼記得車子停在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是荷馬面對的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色顯示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒受損 , 像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你記不得東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文的 「 海馬 」 , 它就像這樣 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元通過互相連接傳遞電脈衝或電突突突 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片非常緊密的細胞組成 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠在尋找食物時的個別神經元
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們正在記錄一個單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體內記錄 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小股電力 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到這神經元知道老鼠在環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送電刺激 , 傳送訊號給大腦其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以讓神經元發射的速度成為動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄許多不同的神經元 , 我們可以看到當動物在不同環境的不同區域時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 如同這個方形的方形方形方形方形方形方形的神經元 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起形成了一張大腦的地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被人類記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時需要大腦的電訊活動
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮上開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	而在牠們河馬體內的位置細胞會發射 , 變得很活躍 , 每當牠們經過某個特定的小鎮時 , 就會開始發射電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 安慰劑細胞如何知道環境中的老鼠或人的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界非常重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方的那一隻會發出訊號 , 像是老鼠在箱子的牆壁之間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子擴大 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這一道牆 , 會在靠近南方時發火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞就會在任何地方被激發 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 , 都會被激發 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這項預測能感應到你周圍各個邊界的距離和方向 , 擴展建築等等 , 對海馬體來說 , 特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 針對海馬體的輸入值 , 發現在海馬體中的哪個專案 , 對於偵測邊界或邊緣的確會做出反應 , 尤其是在探測老鼠或老鼠時 , 該專案的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 它會被激發 , 不論是動物走向東邊 , 或是邊界 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或圓形的牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 桌子的邊緣都會被激發 , 動物會到處跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會被激發 , 不論是在南方的邊緣 , 不論是桌子邊緣或是牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子間的縫隙 , 會被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在哪裡探索 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 比如這個簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 去觀察他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回到環境中 , 它們通常很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變的 , 改變了環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的國旗代表著交叉點在一個小平方的環境中 , 如果你問人們它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟被伸展的方式完全一樣 , 讓位置細胞被激發出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記住了旗子的位置 , 透過儲存位置細胞的激發模式 , 然後你就可以藉由四處移動 , 來找到符合目前位置細胞的激發模式 , 以儲存位置細胞的激發模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會讓你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在移動的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些有限的路徑--或許我們會停車--我們會知道--因為我們自己的動作--我們可以整合這條路--就像我們回去的方向一樣 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從所謂的網格細胞得到這種路徑整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞再次被發現 , 輸入海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞會在一系列不同位置的激發 , 以驚人的三角形網格呈現在整個環境中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄數個格子細胞 , 這裡每個格子上都有類似發射模式的格子 , 每個細胞的激發模式 , 相對於其他細胞 , 會稍微移位 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的在這個格子上發出綠色的 , 藍色的在這個 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 整合起來 , 老鼠可以在環境中放置一個虛擬的網格 , 有點像地圖上的緯度和長途線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電子活動可以從這些細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 以追蹤它的所在位置 , 讓它可以用它自己的動作 , 來知道它在環境中的哪個位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有電網細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有像電網的激發模式有相同的對稱軸 , 如同電網 , 橘色的相同方向圖 , 表示大腦中特定區域的所有電網活動 , 應該根據我們在這個六個方向之間的移動 , 或在中間的六個方向的移動 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人放進核磁共振成像掃描儀中 , 讓他們玩一些電玩遊戲 , 像是我剛給你們看的那個 , 尋找信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 在人類的腦內皮質也就是老鼠腦內的網格細胞 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子在哪裡 , 以距離和方向 , 來延伸建築物和界線 , 讓他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞的激發出來 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出汽車停車場的路徑 , 可以在網格細胞激發中呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都能讓位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動來返回停車位的位置 , 找到目前在他腦中的位置 , 和儲存車子停車位置位置細胞的激發模式做匹配 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個位置 , 和視覺提示不一樣 , 比如他的車子是否真的在那 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被用完了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡取得它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似網格的激發模式 , 我們會在一連串的位置上看到它 , 當我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 它總是很活躍 , 比如說 , 上次你參加婚禮時 , 會記得它 。
